Page 1
Turkey 
Coordinates: [URL: "https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Turkey&params=39_N_35_E_type:city"] 39°N 35°E
Turkey (Turkish: Türkiye [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Turkish"] [ˈtyɾcije]), officially the Republic of Türkiye
(Turkish: Türkiye Cumhuriyeti [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Turkish"] [ˈtyɾcije dʒumˈhuːɾijeti] (  listen)),  is a
 transcontinental country located mainly on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolia"] Anatolian Peninsula in
 Western Asia, with a small portion on the Balkan Peninsula in Southeast
Europe. It shares borders with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Sea"] Black Sea to the north; [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_(country)"] Georgia to the
northeast; Armenia, Azerbaijan, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran"] Iran to the east; [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq"] Iraq to the southeast;
 Syria and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea"] Mediterranean Sea to the south; the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aegean_Sea"] Aegean Sea to the west;
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greece"] Greece and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgaria"] Bulgaria to the northwest. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus"] Cyprus is located off the south
coast. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_people"] Turks form the vast majority of the nation's population and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurds"] Kurds are
 the largest minority.[4] Ankara is Turkey's capital, while Istanbul is its largest
city and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_centre"] financial centre.
One of the world's earliest permanently [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Settler"] settled regions, present-day Turkey
was home to important [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic"] Neolithic sites like [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe"] Göbekli Tepe, and was inhabited
by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civilization"] ancient civilisations including the Hattians, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolian_peoples"] Anatolian peoples,
 Mycenaean Greeks and others.[11][12][13][14] Following the conquests of
 Alexander the Great which started the Hellenistic period, most of the ancient
regions in modern Turkey were culturally Hellenised, which continued
during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire"] Byzantine era.[12][15] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seljuk_Empire"] Seljuk Turks began migrating in the
 11th century, and the Sultanate of Rum ruled Anatolia until the Mongol
invasion in 1243, when it disintegrated into small [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolian_beyliks"] Turkish principalities.[16]
 Beginning in the late 13th century, the Ottomans united the principalities and
conquered the Balkans, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkification"] Turkification of Anatolia increased during
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire"] Ottoman period. After [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehmed_II"] Mehmed II [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople"] conquered [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantinople"] Constantinople (Istanbul)
in 1453, Ottoman expansion continued under [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selim_I"] Selim I. During the reign of
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transformation_of_the_Ottoman_Empire"] Suleiman the Magnificent, the Ottoman Empire became a global
 power.[11][17][18] From the late 18th century onwards, the empire's power
 declined with a gradual loss of territories.[19] Mahmud II started a period of
modernisation in the early 19th century.[20] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution"] Young Turk Revolution of
 1908 restricted the authority of the Sultan and restored the Ottoman
 Parliament after a 30-year suspension, ushering the empire into a multi-party
period.[21][22] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1913_Ottoman_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat"] 1913 coup d'état put the country under the control of the
 Three Pashas, who facilitated the Empire's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_entry_into_World_War_I"] entry into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I"] World War I as part of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Powers"] Central Powers in 1914. During the war, the Ottoman government
committed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Ottoman_genocides"] genocides against its Armenian, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_genocide"] Greek and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assyrian_genocide"] Assyrian
subjects.[a][25] After its defeat in the war, the Ottoman Empire was
partitioned.[26]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence"] Turkish War of Independence against the occupying [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I"] Allied Powers
resulted in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abolition_of_the_Ottoman_sultanate"] abolition of the Sultanate on 1 November 1922, the signing of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Lausanne"] Treaty of Lausanne (which superseded the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres"] Treaty of Sèvres) on 24 July
1923 and the proclamation of the Republic on 29 October 1923. With the
 reforms initiated by the country's first president, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk"] Mustafa Kemal Atatürk,
Turkey became a secular, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unitary_state"] unitary and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_republic"] parliamentary republic. Turkey played
a prominent role in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korean_War"] Korean War and joined [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO"] NATO in 1952. The country
endured several military [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coup"] coups in the latter half of the 20th century. The
economy was liberalised in the 1980s, leading to stronger economic growth
and political stability. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_republic"] parliamentary republic was replaced with a
 presidential system by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_Turkish_constitutional_referendum"] referendum in 2017.
Turkey is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_power"] regional power and a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newly_industrialized_country"] newly industrialized country,[27] with a
geopolitically strategic location.[28] Its economy, which is classified among
 the emerging and growth-leading economies, is the twentieth-largest in the
world by nominal GDP, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)"] eleventh-largest by PPP. It is a charter
member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations"] United Nations, an early member of NATO, the IMF, and the
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank"] World Bank, and a founding member of the OECD, OSCE, BSEC, OIC,

Europe in 1950, Turkey became an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara_Agreement"] associate member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Economic_Community"] EEC in 1963,
joined the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union"] EU Customs Union in 1995, and started [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accession_of_Turkey_to_the_European_Union"] accession negotiations
with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union"] European Union in 2005. Turkey has a rich cultural legacy shaped
by centuries of history and the influence of the various peoples that have
 inhabited its territory over several millennia; it is home to 19 UNESCO
World Heritage Sites and is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Tourism_rankings"] among the most visited countries in the world.

Page 3
Name
The English name of Turkey (from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Latin"] Medieval Latin Turchia/Turquia[29]) means "land of the Turks". [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English"] Middle English usage of
Turkye is evidenced in an early work by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaucer"] Chaucer called [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Book_of_the_Duchess"] The Book of the Duchess (c. 1369). The phrase land of Torke is used in the
15th-century [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Digby_Conversion_of_Saint_Paul"] Digby Mysteries. Later usages can be found in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Dunbar"] Dunbar poems, the 16th century [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manipulus_Vocabulorum"] Manipulus Vocabulorum (Turkie)
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francis_Bacon"] Francis Bacon's Sylva Sylvarum (Turky). The modern spelling Turkey dates back to at least 1719.[30]
The name of Turkey appeared in the Western sources after the crusades.[31] In the 14th-century Arab sources, turkiyya is usually
contrasted with turkmaniyya (Turkomania), probably to be understood as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oghuz_Turks"] Oghuz in a broad sense.[32] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_Battuta"] Ibn Battuta, in the 1330s
introduces the region as barr al-Turkiyya al-ma'ruf bi-bilad al-Rum ("the Turkish land known as the lands of Rum").[33] The
disintegration of the country after [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I"] World War I revived [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_nationalism"] Turkish nationalism, and the Türkler için Türkiye ("Turkey for the Turks")
sentiment rose up. With the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Alexandropol"] Treaty of Alexandropol signed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_the_Grand_National_Assembly"] Government of the Grand National Assembly with Armenia, the
name of Türkiye entered international documents for the first time. In the treaty signed with Afghanistan, the expression Devlet-i
Aliyye-i Türkiyye ("Sublime Turkish State") was used, likened to the Ottoman Empire's name.[31]
In January 2020, the Turkish Exporters' Assembly (TİM) — the umbrella organisation of Turkish exports — announced that it
would use "Made in Turkiye" on all its labels in a bid to standardise branding and the identity of Turkish businesses on the
international stage, using the term 'Turkiye' across all languages around the world.[34]
In December 2021, President Recep Tayyip Erdoğan issued a circular calling for exports to be labelled "Made in Türkiye". The
circular also stated that in relation to other governmental communications "necessary sensitivity will be shown on the use of the
phrase 'Türkiye' instead of phrases such as 'Turkey', 'Türkei', 'Turquie' etc."[35][36] The reason given in the circular for preferring
Türkiye was that it "represents and expresses the culture, civilisation, and values of the Turkish nation in the best way". According
to Turkish state broadcaster [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TRT_World"] TRT World, it was also to avoid a pejorative association with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey_(bird)"] turkey, the bird.[34] It was reported in
 January 2022 that the government planned to register Türkiye with the United Nations.[37] Minister of Foreign Affairs Mevlüt
Çavuşoğlu sent letters to the UN and other international organisations on 31 May 2022 requesting that they use Türkiye. The UN
agreed and implemented the request immediately.[38][39] Erdoğan also announced that [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Airlines"] Turkish Airlines would commence
international operations under its Turkish name Türk Hava Yolları, based on the name change of the country.[40]
History
Prehistory of Anatolia and Eastern Thrace
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolia"] Anatolian peninsula, comprising most of modern Turkey, is one of the oldest
permanently settled regions in the world. Various [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Anatolians"] ancient Anatolian populations have lived
in Anatolia, from at least the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic"] Neolithic until the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic_civilization"] Hellenistic period.[12] Many of these
 peoples spoke the Anatolian languages, a branch of the larger Indo-European language
family:[42] and, given the antiquity of the Indo-European [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hittite_language"] Hittite and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luwian_language"] Luwian languages,
 some scholars have proposed Anatolia as the hypothetical centre from which the Indo-
European languages radiated.[43] The European part of Turkey, called [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Thrace"] Eastern Thrace, has
Some [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henge"] henges at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe"] Göbekli Tepe were
erected as far back as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe#Layer_III"] 9600 BC, 
also been inhabited since at least forty thousand years ago, and is known to have been in
the Neolithic era by about 6000 BC.[13]
predating those of Stonehenge,
England, by over seven millennia.[41]  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe"] Göbekli Tepe is the site of the oldest known man-made religious structure, a temple dating
to circa 10,000 BC,[41] while [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%87atalh%C3%B6y%C3%BCk"] Çatalhöyük is a very large Neolithic and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chalcolithic"] Chalcolithic
settlement in southern Anatolia, which existed from approximately 7500 BC to 5700 BC. It
is the largest and best-preserved Neolithic site found to date and is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site"] UNESCO World Heritage Site.[44] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neval%C4%B1_%C3%87ori"] Nevalı Çori was an early
 Neolithic settlement on the middle Euphrates, in Şanlıurfa. Urfa Man statue is dated c. 9000 BC to the period of the Pre-Pottery
Neolithic, and is considered as "the oldest naturalistic life-sized sculpture of a human".[45] It is considered as contemporaneous with
the sites of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6bekli_Tepe"] Göbekli Tepe. The settlement of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Troy"] Troy started in the Neolithic Age and continued into the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Age"] Iron Age.[46]
The earliest recorded inhabitants of Anatolia were the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hattians"] Hattians and Hurrians, non-Indo-European peoples who inhabited central
and eastern Anatolia, respectively, as early as c. 2300 BC. Indo-European [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hittites"] Hittites came to Anatolia and gradually absorbed the
Hattians and Hurrians c. 2000–1700 BC. The first major empire in the area was founded by the Hittites, from the 18th through the
13th century BC. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assyria"] Assyrians conquered and settled parts of southeastern Turkey as early as 1950 BC until the year 612 BC,[47]
although they [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assyrian_continuity"] have remained a minority in the region, namely in Hakkari, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%9E%C4%B1rnak_Province"] Şırnak and Mardin.[48]
 Urartu re-emerged in Assyrian inscriptions in the 9th century BC as a powerful northern rival of Assyria.[49] Following the collapse
of the Hittite empire c. 1180 BC, the Phrygians, an Indo-European people, achieved ascendancy in Anatolia until their kingdom
was destroyed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cimmerians"] Cimmerians in the 7th century BC.[50] Starting from 714 BC, Urartu shared the same fate and dissolved in
590 BC,[51] when it was conquered by the Medes. The most powerful of Phrygia's successor states were Lydia, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caria"] Caria and Lycia.
Page 4
 Sardis was an ancient city at the location of modern Sart in Western Turkey. The city
 served as the capital of the ancient kingdom of Lydia. As one of the seven churches of
 Asia, it was addressed in the Book of Revelation in the New Testament,[52] The Lydian
Lion coins were made of electrum, a naturally occurring alloy of gold and silver but of
variable precious metal value. During the reign of King [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croesus"] Croesus that the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metallurgist"] metallurgists of
Sardis discovered the secret of separating [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gold"] gold from silver, thereby producing both metals
of a purity never known before.[53]
Antiquity
Starting around 1200 BC, the coast of Anatolia was heavily settled by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aeolians"] Aeolian and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ionians"] Ionian
Greeks. Numerous important [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polis"] cities were founded by these colonists, such as Didyma,
Miletus, Ephesus, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smyrna"] Smyrna (now İzmir) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantium"] Byzantium (now Istanbul), the latter founded
by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greeks"] Greek colonists from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megara"] Megara in 657 BC.[54] Some of the most prominent pre-Socratic
philosophers lived in the city of Miletus. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thales_of_Miletus"] Thales of Miletus (c. 624 BCE – c. 546 BCE)
considered as first philosopher in the Greek tradition. [55][56] and he is otherwise
historically recognized as the first individual known to have entertained and engaged in
 scientific philosophy.[57][58] In Miletus, he is followed by two other significant pre-
Socratic philosophers [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anaximander"] Anaximander (c. 610 BCE – c. 546 BCE) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anaximenes_of_Miletus"] Anaximenes (c. 585
BCE – c. 525 BCE) (known collectively, to modern scholars, as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milesian_school"] Milesian school). 
The Sphinx Gate of Hattusa, the
capital of the Hittites.
Zeus Temple in ancient city of
 Aizanoi belongs to Phrygia.
For several centuries prior to the great [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Persian_Wars"] Persian invasion of Greece, perhaps the very greatest and wealthiest city of the Greek world
was Miletus, which founded more colonies than any other Greek city,[59] particularly in the Black Sea region. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diogenes_the_Cynic"] Diogenes the Cynic
was one of the founders of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cynicism_(philosophy)"] Cynic philosophy born in one of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ionians"] Ionian colonies [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinop,_Turkey"] Sinope on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Sea"] Black Sea coast of Anatolia in 412.
[60]
 Trojan War took place in the ancient city of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Troy"] Troy by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaeans_(Homer)"] Achaeans (Greeks) after [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_(mythology)"] Paris of
Troy took [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helen_of_Troy"] Helen from her husband Menelaus, king of Sparta. The war is one of the most
important events in Greek mythology and has been narrated through many works of
 Greek literature, most notably [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homer"] Homer's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iliad"] Iliad.  Whether there is any historical reality
behind the Trojan War remains an open question. Those who believe that the stories of
the Trojan War are derived from a specific historical conflict usually date it to the 12th or
11th century BC, often preferring the dates given by Eratosthenes, 1194–1184 BC, which
roughly correspond to archaeological evidence of a catastrophic burning of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Troy_VII"] Troy VII,[65]
and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Bronze_Age_collapse"] Late Bronze Age collapse.
The first state that was called [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenia"] Armenia by neighbouring peoples was the state of the
 Armenian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orontid_dynasty"] Orontid dynasty, which included parts of what is now eastern Turkey
beginning in the 6th century BC. In Northwest Turkey, the most significant tribal group in
Thrace was the Odyrisians, founded by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teres_I"] Teres I.[66]
All of modern-day Turkey was conquered by the Persian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire"] Achaemenid Empire during the
6th century BC.[67] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Persian_Wars"] Greco-Persian Wars started when the Greek city states on the
coast of Anatolia rebelled against Persian rule in 499 BC.
 Artemisia I of Caria was a queen of the ancient Greek city-state of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halicarnassus"] Halicarnassus and she
fought as an ally of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xerxes_I"] Xerxes I, King of Persia against the independent Greek city states
during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Persian_invasion_of_Greece"] second Persian invasion of Greece. She personally commanded her
contribution of five ships at the naval [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Artemisium"] battle of Artemisium in 480 BC.[68][69][70]
The territory of Turkey later fell to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_the_Great"] Alexander the Great in 334 BC,[71] which led to
increasing cultural homogeneity and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenization"] Hellenization in the area.[12] Following Alexander's
death in 323 BC, Anatolia was subsequently divided into a number of small Hellenistic
kingdoms, all of which became part of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Republic"] Roman Republic by the mid-1st century
BC.[72] The process of Hellenization that began with Alexander's conquest accelerated
under Roman rule, and by the early centuries of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Era"] Christian Era, the local Anatolian
 languages and cultures had become extinct, being largely replaced by ancient Greek
language and culture.[15][73] From the 1st century BC up to the 3rd century CE, large
parts of modern-day Turkey were contested between the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire"] Romans and neighbouring
 Parthians through the frequent [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman-Parthian_Wars"] Roman-Parthian Wars. 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theatre_at_Halicarnassus"] Theatre at Halicarnassus (modern
Bodrum) was built in the 4th century
BC by Mausolus, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire"] Persian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satrap"] satrap
 (governor) of Caria. The Mausoleum at
 Halicarnassus was one of the Seven
Wonders of the Ancient World.[61][62]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_of_Celsus"] Library of Celsus in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ephesus"] Ephesus was
built by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire"] Romans in 114–117.[63]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_of_Artemis"] Temple of Artemis in Ephesus,
built by king [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croesus"] Croesus of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lydia"] Lydia in the
6th century BCE, was one of the
 Seven Wonders of the Ancient
World.[64]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul"]
Page 5
 Galatia was an ancient area in the highlands of central Anatolia inhabited by the Celts. The terms "Galatians" came to be used by
the Greeks for the three Celtic peoples of Anatolia: the Tectosages, the Trocmii, and the Tolistobogii.[74][75] By the 1st century BC
the Celts had become so [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenization"] Hellenized that some Greek writers called them Hellenogalatai (Ἑλληνογαλάται).[76] Galatia was named
after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gauls"] Gauls from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thrace"] Thrace (cf. Tylis), who settled here and became a small transient foreign tribe in the 3rd century BC, following
the supposed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gallic_invasion_of_the_Balkans"] Gallic invasion of the Balkans in 279 BC.
 Kingdom of Pontus was a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic_period"] Hellenistic kingdom, centered in the historical region of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pontus_(region)"] Pontus and ruled by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mithridatic_dynasty"] Mithridatic dynasty of
 Persian origin,[77][78][79][80] which may have been directly related to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darius_I"] Darius the Great and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_dynasty"] Achaemenid dynasty.[81][80] The
kingdom was proclaimed by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mithridates_I_of_Pontus"] Mithridates I in 281 BC and lasted until its conquest by the Roman Republic in 63 BC. The Kingdom
of Pontus reached its largest extent under [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mithridates_VI"] Mithridates VI the Great, who conquered Colchis, Cappadocia, Bithynia, the Greek
colonies of the Tauric Chersonesos. After a long struggle with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire"] Rome in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mithridatic_Wars"] Mithridatic Wars, Pontus was defeated.
All territories corresponding to modern Turkey eventually fell into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire"] Roman Empire’s control.
Early Christian and Roman period
According to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acts_of_Apostles"] Acts of Apostles,[83] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antioch"] Antioch (now Antakya), a city in southern Turkey,
is where followers of Jesus were [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_Christianity"] first called "Christians" and became very quickly an
important center of Christianity.[84][85] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle"] Paul the Apostle traveled to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ephesus"] Ephesus and stayed
there for almost three years, probably working there as a tentmaker,[86] as he had done
when he stayed in Corinth. He is claimed to have performed numerous miracles, healing
people and casting out demons, and he apparently organized missionary activity in other
regions.[87] Paul left [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ephesus"] Ephesus after an attack from a local silversmith resulted in a pro-
 Artemis riot involving most of the city.[87]
In the year 123, Emperor [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hadrian"] Hadrian traveled to Anatolia. Numerous monuments erected for
his arrival and he met his lover [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antinous"] Antinous from Bithynia.[88] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hadrian"] Hadrian focused on the
Greek revival and built several temples and improved the cities. Cyzicus, Pergamon,
Smyrna, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ephesus"] Ephesus and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sardes"] Sardes were promoted as regional centres for the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_cult_(ancient_Rome)"] Imperial cult
([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neocorate"] neocoros) during this period.[89] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire"] Byzantine Empire in 555 under
 Justinian the Great, at its greatest
extent since the fall of the Western
Roman Empire.
Byzantine period
In 324, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_I"] Constantine I chose Byzantium to be the new capital of the Roman Empire,
renaming it [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Rome"] New Rome. Under Constantine, Christianity did not become the exclusive
 religion of the state, but enjoyed imperial preference since he supported it with generous Originally a church, then a mosque,
privileges. Following the death of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theodosius_I"] Theodosius I in 395 and the permanent division of the
Roman Empire between his two sons, the city, which would popularly come to be known
as Constantinople, became the capital of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire"] Eastern Roman Empire. This empire, which
would later be branded by historians as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire"] Byzantine Empire, ruled most of the territory
of present-day Turkey until the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages"] Late Middle Ages;[90] although the eastern regions 
later a museum, and now a mosque
again, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hagia_Sophia"] Hagia Sophia in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul"] Istanbul
was built by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire"] Byzantine emperor
 Justinian I in 532–537 AD.[82]
remained firmly in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasanian"] Sasanian hands until the first half of the 7th century CE. The frequent
 Byzantine-Sassanid Wars, a continuation of the centuries-long [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman-Persian_Wars"] Roman-Persian Wars, took place in various parts of present-day
Turkey between the 4th and 7th centuries CE. Several [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecumenical_councils"] ecumenical councils of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_Church"] early Church were held in cities located in
present-day Turkey, including the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Council_of_Nicaea"] First Council of Nicaea (Iznik) in 325, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Council_of_Constantinople"] First Council of Constantinople (Istanbul) in 381, the
 Council of Ephesus in 431, and the Council of Chalcedon (Kadıköy) in 451.[91] During most of its existence, the Byzantine
Empire was one of the most powerful economic, cultural, and military forces in Europe.[92]
Seljuks and the Ottoman Empire
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seljuq_dynasty"] House of Seljuk originated from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C4%B1n%C4%B1k_(tribe)"] Kınık branch of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oghuz_Turks"] Oghuz Turks who resided on the periphery of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_history#Abbasids_-_%22Islamic_Golden_Age%22"] Muslim world, in
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oghuz_Yabgu_State"] Yabgu Khaganate of the Oğuz confederacy, to the north of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_Sea"] Caspian and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aral_Sea"] Aral Seas, in the 9th century.[93] In the 10th
 century, the Seljuks started migrating from their ancestral homeland into Persia, which became the administrative core of the Great
Seljuk Empire, after its foundation by Tughril.[94]
In the latter half of the 11th century, the Seljuk Turks began penetrating into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Armenia"] medieval Armenia and the eastern regions of Anatolia.
In 1071, the Seljuks defeated the Byzantines at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Manzikert"] Battle of Manzikert, starting the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkification"] Turkification process in the area; the Turkish
language and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam"] Islam were introduced to Armenia and Anatolia, gradually spreading throughout the region. The slow transition from
a predominantly [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christians"] Christian and Greek-speaking Anatolia to a predominantly [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim"] Muslim and Turkish-speaking one was underway. The
 Mevlevi Order of dervishes, which was established in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Konya"] Konya during the 13th century by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sufi"] Sufi poet [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celaleddin_Rumi"] Celaleddin Rumi, played a
significant role in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamization"] Islamization of the diverse people of Anatolia who had previously been Hellenized.[96][97] Thus, alongside
Page 6
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Seljuk_Empire"] Great Seljuk Empire in 1092,
upon the death of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malik_Shah_I"] Malik Shah I[95] 
 the Turkification of the territory, the culturally Persianized Seljuks set the basis for a Turko-
Persian principal culture in Anatolia,[98] which their eventual successors, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_the_Ottoman_Empire"] the Ottomans,
would take over.[99][100]In 1243, the Seljuk armies were defeated by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_Empire"] Mongols at the
 Battle of Köse Dağ, causing the Seljuk Empire's power to slowly disintegrate. In its wake,
one of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolian_beyliks"] Turkish principalities governed by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_I"] Osman I would evolve over the next 200
years into the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire"] Ottoman Empire. The Ottomans completed their conquest of the Byzantine
Empire by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople"] capturing its capital, Constantinople, in 1453: their commander thenceforth
being known as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehmed_the_Conqueror"] Mehmed the Conqueror.
In 1514, Sultan [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selim_I"] Selim I (1512–1520) successfully expanded the empire's southern and
eastern borders by defeating Shah [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ismail_I"] Ismail I of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_dynasty"] Safavid dynasty in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Chaldiran"] Battle of Chaldiran.
In 1517, Selim I expanded Ottoman rule into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Algeria"] Algeria and Egypt, and created a naval
presence in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Sea"] Red Sea. Subsequently, a contest started between the Ottoman and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portuguese_Empire"] Portuguese
 empires to become the dominant sea power in the Indian Ocean, with a number of naval
battles in the Red Sea, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Sea"] Arabian Sea and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf"] Persian Gulf. The Portuguese presence in the
Indian Ocean was perceived as a threat to the Ottoman monopoly over the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silk_Road"] ancient trade routes
between [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Asia"] East Asia and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Europe"] Western Europe. Despite the increasingly prominent European
presence, the Ottoman Empire's trade with the east continued to flourish until the second half
of the 18th century.[103]
The Ottoman Empire's power and prestige peaked in the 16th and 17th centuries, particularly
during the reign of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent"] Suleiman the Magnificent, who personally instituted major legislative
changes relating to society, education, taxation and criminal law.
 Topkapı and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace"] Dolmabahçe palaces
were the primary residences of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire"] Ottoman [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_the_Ottoman_Empire"] Sultans in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul"] Istanbul 
The empire was often at odds with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire"] Holy Roman Empire in its steady advance towards
 Central Europe through the Balkans and the southern part of the Polish–Lithuanian
Commonwealth.[104]
between 1465 to 1856[101] and
1856 to 1922,[102] respectively. 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Navy"] Ottoman Navy contended with
several Holy Leagues, such as those in
1538, 1571, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_League_(1684)"] 1684 and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_League_(1717)"] 1717 (composed
primarily of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habsburg_Spain"] Habsburg Spain, the
 Republic of Genoa, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Venice"] Republic of Venice, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller"] Knights of St. John, the
 Papal States, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Tuscany"] Grand Duchy of Tuscany and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Savoy"] Duchy of Savoy), for the
control of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea"] Mediterranean Sea.
In the east, the Ottomans were often at war with Safavid Persia over conflicts
stemming from territorial disputes or religious differences between the 16th
and 18th centuries.[105] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman-Persian_Wars"] Ottoman wars with Persia continued as the
Zand, Afsharid, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qajar_dynasty"] Qajar dynasties succeeded the Safavids in Iran, until the
 first half of the 19th century.
Even further east, there was an extension of the Habsburg-Ottoman conflict,
in that the Ottomans also had to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_expedition_to_Aceh"] send soldiers to their farthest and easternmost
vassal and territory, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aceh_Sultanate"] Aceh Sultanate[106][107] in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Asia"] Southeast Asia, to defend
it from European colonizers as well as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_de_Salcedo"] Latino invaders who had crossed
from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_America"] Latin America and had Christianized the formerly Muslim-dominated
Philippines.[108] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna"] Second Ottoman Siege of Vienna in 1683 (the
 First Siege was in 1529) initiated the Great Turkish
 War (1683–1699) between the Ottomans and a Holy
League of European states.
 From the 16th to the early 20th centuries, the Ottoman Empire also fought
twelve wars with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia"] Russian Tsardom and Empire. These were initially about Ottoman territorial expansion and consolidation in
southeastern and eastern Europe; but starting from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1768%E2%80%931774)"] Russo-Turkish War (1768–1774), they became more about the survival of
the Ottoman Empire, which had begun to lose its strategic territories on the northern [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Sea"] Black Sea coast to the advancing Russians.
From the second half of the 18th century onwards, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decline_of_the_Ottoman_Empire"] Ottoman Empire began to decline. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanzimat"] Tanzimat reforms, initiated by
 Mahmud II just before his death in 1839, aimed to modernise the Ottoman state in line with the progress that had been made in
Western Europe. The efforts of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midhat_Pasha"] Midhat Pasha during the late Tanzimat era led the Ottoman [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_constitution_of_1876"] constitutional movement of 1876, which
 introduced the First Constitutional Era, but these efforts proved to be inadequate in most fields, and failed to stop the dissolution of
the empire.[109]
As the empire gradually shrank in size, military power and wealth; especially after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Eastern_Crisis"] Ottoman economic crisis and default in
1875[110] which led to uprisings in the Balkan provinces that culminated in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878)"] Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878); many Balkan
Muslims migrated to the Empire's heartland in Anatolia,[111][112] along with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circassians"] Circassians fleeing the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian%E2%80%93Circassian_War"] Russian conquest of the
Caucasus. According to some estimates, up to 1.5 million Muslim [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circassians"] Circassians died during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circassian_genocide"] Circassian genocide, the survivors
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Europe"]
Page 7
 seek refugee in Ottoman Empire. The decline of the Ottoman Empire led to a rise in nationalist sentiment among its various subject
peoples, leading to increased ethnic tensions which occasionally burst into violence, such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamidian_massacres"] Hamidian massacres of Armenians,
which claimed up to 300,000 lives.[113]
The loss of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rumelia"] Rumelia (Ottoman territories in Europe) with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Balkan_War"] First Balkan War
(1912–1913) was followed by the arrival of millions of Muslim refugees
([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhacir"] muhacir) to Istanbul and Anatolia.[114] Historically, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rumelia_Eyalet"] Rumelia Eyalet and
 Anatolia Eyalet had formed the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Ottoman_Empire"] administrative core of the Ottoman Empire, with
their governors titled [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beylerbey"] Beylerbeyi participating in the Sultan's Divan, so the loss
of all Balkan provinces beyond the Midye-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enez"] Enez border line according to the
 London Conference of 1912–13 and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_London_(1913)"] Treaty of London (1913) was a major
shock for the Ottoman society and led to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1913_Ottoman_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat"] 1913 Ottoman coup d'état. In the
 Second Balkan War (1913) the Ottomans managed to recover their former
capital [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edirne"] Edirne (Adrianople) and its surrounding areas in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Thrace"] East Thrace, which was
formalised with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Constantinople_(1913)"] Treaty of Constantinople (1913).  The 1913 coup d'état
effectively put the country under the control of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three_Pashas"] Three Pashas, making sultans
 Mehmed V and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehmed_VI"] Mehmed VI largely symbolic figureheads with no real political
power.

Kaiser [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_II,_German_Emperor"] Wilhelm II of Germany;
Kaiser and King [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franz_Joseph_I_of_Austria"] Franz Joseph of Austria-

The caption reads:"United Powers Lead to
successfully defended the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dardanelles"] Dardanelles
strait during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gallipoli_campaign"] Gallipoli campaign
(1915–1916) and achieved initial victories against British forces in the first two years of the
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamian_campaign"] Mesopotamian campaign, such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Kut"] Siege of Kut (1915–1916); but the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Revolt"] Arab Revolt
 (1916–1918) turned the tide against the Ottomans in the Middle East. In the Caucasus
Armenian civilians being deported
during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide"] Armenian genocide 
campaign, however, the Russian forces had the upper hand from the beginning, especially
after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Sarikamish"] Battle of Sarikamish (1914–1915). Russian forces advanced into northeastern
Anatolia and controlled the major cities there until retreating from World War I with the
 Treaty of Brest-Litovsk following the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Revolution"] Russian Revolution (1917). During the war, the
empire's Armenian subjects were [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehcir_Law"] deported to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria"] Syria as part of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide"] Armenian genocide. As a result, an estimated 600,000[115] to
 more than 1 million,[115] or up to 1.5 million[116][117][118] Armenians were killed. The Turkish government has refused to
 acknowledge the events as genocide and states that Armenians were only "relocated" from the eastern war zone.[119] Genocidal
campaigns were also committed against the empire's other minority groups such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assyrian_genocide"] Assyrians and Greeks.[120][121][122] The
share of non-Muslims in area within Turkey's current borders declined from 20-22% in 1914, or about 3.3.–3.6 million people, to
 around 3% in 1927.[123] Following the Armistice of Mudros on 30 October 1918, the victorious Allied Powers sought to partition
the Ottoman state through the 1920 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres"] Treaty of Sèvres.[124]
Republic of Turkey 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupation_of_Constantinople"] occupation of Istanbul (1918) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupation_of_Smyrna"] İzmir (1919) by the Allies in the aftermath of World
War I prompted the establishment of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_National_Movement"] Turkish National Movement. Under the leadership
of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk"] Mustafa Kemal Pasha, a military commander who had distinguished himself during the
 Battle of Gallipoli, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence"] Turkish War of Independence (1919–1923) was waged with the aim
of revoking the terms of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres"] Treaty of Sèvres (1920).[125]
By 18 September 1922 the Greek, Armenian and French armies had been expelled,[126]
 Mustafa Kemal Atatürk, founder and
first President of the Turkish
 Republic, with the Liberal Republican
Party leader [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fethi_Okyar"] Fethi Okyar (right) and
Okyar's daughter in Yalova, 13
August 1930. 
and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Provisional_Government"] Turkish Provisional Government in Ankara, which had declared itself the legitimate
government of the country on [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey"] 23 April 1920, started to formalise the legal transition from
the old Ottoman into the new Republican political system. On 1 November 1922, the
Turkish Parliament in Ankara formally [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abolition_of_the_Ottoman_Sultanate"] abolished the Sultanate, thus ending 623 years of
monarchical Ottoman rule. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Lausanne"] Treaty of Lausanne of 24 July 1923, which superseded the
Treaty of Sèvres,[124][125] led to the international recognition of the sovereignty of the
newly formed "Republic of Turkey" as the successor state of the Ottoman Empire, and the
republic was officially proclaimed on 29 October 1923 in Ankara, the country's new
 capital.[127] The Lausanne Convention stipulated a population exchange between Greece
and Turkey, whereby 1.1 million Greeks left Turkey for Greece in exchange for 380,000 Muslims transferred from Greece to
Turkey.[128]
Page 8
 Mustafa Kemal became the republic's first President and subsequently introduced many
reforms. The reforms aimed to transform the old [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Millet_(Ottoman_Empire)"] religion-based and multi-communal
Ottoman [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy"] constitutional monarchy into a Turkish [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nation_state"] nation state that would be governed as a
 parliamentary republic under a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Constitution_of_1924"] secular constitution.[130] With the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surname_Law"] Surname Law of 1934,
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Parliament"] Turkish Parliament bestowed upon Mustafa Kemal the honorific surname "Atatürk"
(Father Turk).[125]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montreux_Convention_Regarding_the_Regime_of_the_Straits"] Montreux Convention (1936) restored Turkey's control over the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Straits"] Turkish Straits,
including the right to militarise the coastlines of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dardanelles"] Dardanelles and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosporus"] Bosporus straits and
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara"] Sea of Marmara, and to block maritime traffic in wartime.[131]
Following the establishment of the Republic of Turkey in 1923, some [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurds"] Kurdish and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zazas"] Zaza
tribes, which were [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feudalism"] feudal (manorial) communities led by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribal_chief"] chieftains ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agha_(title)"] agha) during the
Ottoman period, became discontent about certain aspects of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk%27s_Reforms"] Atatürk's reforms aiming to
 modernise the country, such as secularism (the Sheikh Said rebellion, 1925)[132] and land
reform (the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dersim_rebellion"] Dersim rebellion, 1937–1938),[133] and staged armed revolts that were put
down with military operations. 
Eighteen female [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_of_parliament"] deputies joined the
 Turkish Parliament with the 1935
general elections. Turkish women
 gained the right to vote and to hold
elected office as a mark of the far-
reaching [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk%27s_Reforms"] social changes initiated by
Atatürk.[129]
 İsmet İnönü became Turkey's second President following Atatürk's death on 10 November 1938. On 29 June 1939, the Republic of
Hatay voted in favour of joining Turkey with a referendum. Turkey [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Cairo_Conference"] remained neutral during most of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II"] World War II, but entered the
closing stages of the war on the side of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II"] Allies on 23 February 1945. On 26 June 1945, Turkey became a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Charter"] charter member of the
 United Nations.[134] In the following year, the single-party period in Turkey came to an end, with the first multiparty elections in
1946. In 1950 Turkey became a member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Europe"] Council of Europe.
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democrat_Party_(Turkey,_1946%E2%80%9361)"] Democratic Party established by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cel%C3%A2l_Bayar"] Celâl Bayar won the 1950, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1954_Turkish_general_election"] 1954 and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1957_Turkish_general_election"] 1957 general
elections and stayed in power for a decade, with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adnan_Menderes"] Adnan Menderes as the Prime Minister
and Bayar as the President. After fighting as part of the United Nations forces in the
 Korean War, Turkey joined [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO"] NATO in 1952, becoming a bulwark against Soviet expansion
into the Mediterranean. Turkey subsequently became a founding member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development"] OECD in
1961, and an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara_Agreement"] associate member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Economic_Community"] EEC in 1963.[135]
Roosevelt, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%B0smet_%C4%B0n%C3%B6n%C3%BC"] İnönü and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill"] Churchill at the
 Second Cairo Conference, 1943. 
The country's tumultuous transition to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-party_period_of_the_Republic_of_Turkey"] multiparty democracy was interrupted by military
 coups d'état in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1960_Turkish_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat"] 1960 and 1980, as well as by military memorandums in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1971_Turkish_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat"] 1971 and
1997.[136][137] Between 1960 and the end of the 20th century, the prominent leaders in
 Turkish politics who achieved multiple election victories were Süleyman Demirel, Bülent
Ecevit and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turgut_%C3%96zal"] Turgut Özal. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tansu_%C3%87iller"] Tansu Çiller became the first female prime minister of Turkey in
1993.
Following a decade of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cypriot_intercommunal_violence"] Cypriot intercommunal violence and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1974_Cypriot_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat"] coup in Cyprus on 15 July 1974 staged by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EOKA_B"] EOKA B
paramilitary organisation, which overthrew President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Makarios_III"] Makarios and installed the pro-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enosis"] Enosis (union with Greece) [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikos_Sampson"] Nikos Sampson as
dictator, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_invasion_of_Cyprus"] Turkey invaded Cyprus on 20 July 1974 by unilaterally exercising Article IV in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Guarantee_(1960)"] Treaty of Guarantee (1960), but
without restoring the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Status_quo_ante_bellum"] status quo ante at the end of the military operation.[138] In 1983 the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus"] Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus,
which is recognised only by Turkey, was established.[139] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annan_Plan_for_Cyprus"] Annan Plan for reunifying the island was supported by the majority
of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Cypriots"] Turkish Cypriots, but rejected by the majority of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_Cypriots"] Greek Cypriots, in separate [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_Cypriot_Annan_Plan_referendums"] referendums in 2004. However, negotiations for
solving the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus_dispute"] Cyprus dispute are still ongoing between Turkish Cypriot and Greek Cypriot political leaders.[140]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdish%E2%80%93Turkish_conflict_(1978%E2%80%93present)"] conflict between Turkey and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdistan_Workers%27_Party"] Kurdistan Workers' Party (PKK) (designated a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_designated_terrorist_groups"] terrorist organisation by Turkey, the United
States,[141] and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union"] European Union[142]) has been active since 1984, primarily in the southeast of the country. More than 40,000
people have died as a result of the conflict.[143][144][145] In 1999 PKK's founder [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_%C3%96calan"] Abdullah Öcalan was arrested and sentenced for
 terrorism[141][142] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treason"] treason charges.[146][147] In the past, various [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdish_people"] Kurdish groups have unsuccessfully sought [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_separatism"] separation from
 Turkey to create an independent Kurdish state, while others have more recently pursued provincial autonomy and greater political
and cultural rights for Kurds in Turkey. In the 21st century some reforms have taken place to improve the cultural rights of ethnic
minorities in Turkey, such as the establishment of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TRT_Kurd%C3%AE"] TRT Kurdî, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TRT_Arabi"] TRT Arabi and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TRT_Avaz"] TRT Avaz by the TRT.
Since the liberalisation of the Turkish economy in the 1980s, the country has enjoyed stronger economic growth and greater
political stability.[148] Turkey applied for full membership of the EEC in 1987, joined the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union"] EU Customs Union in 1995 and started
 accession negotiations with the European Union in 2005.[149][150] In a non-binding vote on 13 March 2019, the European
Parliament called on the EU governments to suspend EU accession talks with Turkey, citing violations of human rights and the rule
of law; but the negotiations, effectively on hold since 2018, remain active as of 2020.[151]
In 2013, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013_protests_in_Turkey"] widespread protests erupted in many Turkish provinces, sparked by a plan to demolish [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gezi_Park"] Gezi Park but soon growing into
general anti-government dissent.[152] On 15 July 2016, an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_Turkish_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt"] unsuccessful coup attempt tried to oust the government.[153] As a
reaction to the failed coup d'état, the government carried out [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Turkish_purges"] mass purges.[154][155]
Page 9
 Between 9 October and 25 November 2019, Turkey invaded north-eastern
Syria.[156][157][158]
Administrative divisions
Turkey has a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unitary_state"] unitary structure in terms of administration and this aspect is one of the
most important factors shaping the Turkish public administration. When three powers
(executive, legislative and judiciary) are taken into account as the main functions of
the state, local administrations have little power. Turkey does not have a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federalism"] federal
system, and the provinces are subordinate to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_government"] central government in Ankara. Local
administrations were established to provide services in place and the government is
represented by the province governors (vali) and town governors (kaymakam). Other 
 Anıtkabir, the mausoleum of Mustafa
Kemal Atatürk in Ankara, is visited by
large crowds every year during national
holidays, such as Republic Day on 29
October.
senior public officials are also appointed by the central government instead of the
mayors (belediye başkanı) or elected by constituents.[159] Turkish municipalities have local legislative bodies (belediye meclisi) for
decision-making on municipal issues.
Within this unitary framework, Turkey is subdivided into 81 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provinces_of_Turkey"] provinces (il or vilayet) for administrative purposes. Each province is
divided into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Districts_of_Turkey"] districts (ilçe), for a total of 973 districts.[160] Turkey is also subdivided into 7 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geographical_regions_of_Turkey"] regions (bölge) and 21 subregions for
geographic, demographic and economic purposes; this does not refer to an administrative division.
