Government and politics
Turkey is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_system"] presidential [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic"] republic within a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-party_period_of_the_Republic_of_Turkey"] multi-party system.[161] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Turkey"] current constitution was approved by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_Turkish_constitutional_referendum"] referendum in 1982,
which determines the government's structure, lays forth the ideals and standards of the state's conduct, and sets out the state's
responsibility to its citizens. Furthermore, the constitution specifies the people's rights and obligations, as well as principles for the
delegation and exercise of sovereignty that belongs to the people of Turkey.[162]
 In the Turkish unitary system, citizens are subject to three levels of government: national, provincial, and local. The local
government's duties are commonly split between [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Municipal_corporation"] municipal governments and districts, in which executive and legislative officials
are elected by a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plurality_voting_system"] plurality vote of citizens by district. Turkey is subdivided into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provinces_of_Turkey"] 81 provinces for administrative purposes. Each
province is divided into districts, for a total of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_districts_in_Turkey"] 973 districts.
The government, regulated by a system of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_powers"] separation of powers as defined by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Turkey"] constitution of Turkey, comprises three branches:
Legislative: The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicameralism"] unicameral [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey"] Parliament makes law, debates and adopts the budget bills, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declaration_of_war"] declares war, approves
treaties, proclaims [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amnesty"] amnesty and pardon, and has the power of impeachment, by which it can remove sitting
members of the government.[163]
Executive: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Turkey"] The president is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commander-in-chief"] commander-in-chief of the military, can veto [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_(law)"] legislative bills before they become
law (subject to parliamentary override), can issue [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decree"] presidential decrees on matters regarding executive power with
exception of fundamental rights, individual rights and certain political rights (parliamentary laws prevail
presidential decrees), and appoints the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_Turkey"] members of the Cabinet and other officers, who administer and enforce
national laws and policies.[164]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trabzon_Province"]
Page 10
Judicial: The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Turkey"] Constitutional Court (for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutionality"] constitutional adjudication and review of
individual applications concerning human rights), the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Court_of_Cassation_of_Turkey"] Court of Cassation (final
decision maker in ordinary judiciary), the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Council_of_State"] Council of State (final decision maker
in administrative judiciary) and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Court_of_Jurisdictional_Disputes"] Court of Jurisdictional Disputes (for resolving
the disputes between courts for constitutional jurisdiction) are the four
organizations that are described by the Constitution as supreme courts. The
judges of the Constitutional Court are appointed by the president and the
parliament.[165]
The Parliament has 600 voting members, each representing a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constituency"] constituency for a five-year term.
Parliamentairy seats are distributed among the provinces by population, conform with the
census apportionment. The president is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_presidential_elections"] elected by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct_vote"] direct vote and serves a five-year term. The
president can't run for re-elections after two terms of five-year. If the Parliament decides to
prematurely renew the presidential elections during the second term of the President, he or she
may run for a third presidential term. Elections for the Parliament and presidential elections are
held on the same day. The Constitutional Court is composed of fifteen members. A member is
elected for a term of twelve years and can't be reelected. The members of the Constitutional
Court are obliged to retire when they are over the age of sixty-five.[166] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey"] Grand National Assembly,
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legislative_chamber"] legislative chamber in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara"] Ankara
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_Complex_(Turkey)"] Presidential Complex,
residence and workplace of the
 President of Turkey
Parties and elections
Elections in Turkey are held for six functions of government: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_presidential_elections"] presidential elections (national),
 parliamentary elections (national),  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropolitan_municipalities_in_Turkey"] municipality mayors (local),  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_districts_in_Turkey"] district mayors (local),
 provincial or [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Turkey"] municipal council members (local) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhtar_(title)"] muhtars (local). Apart from elections,
 referenda are also held occasionally. 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Turkey"] Constitutional Court, where
the nation's highest court for
constitutional review sits
Every Turkish citizen who has turned 18 has the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suffrage"] right to vote and stand as a candidate at
elections. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_suffrage"] Universal suffrage for both sexes has been applied throughout Turkey since 1934 and
before most countries. In Turkey, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voter_turnout"] turnout rates of both local and general elections are high compared
 to many other countries, which usually stands higher than 80 percent.[167] There are 600 members of
parliament who are elected for a five-year term by a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Party-list_proportional_representation"] party-list proportional representation system
from 88 electoral districts. The Constitutional Court can strip the public financing of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Turkey"] political parties
that it deems [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secularism_in_Turkey"] anti-secular or having ties to terrorism, or ban their existence altogether.[168][169] The
 electoral threshold for political parties at national level is seven percent of the votes.[170] Smaller
parties can avoid the electoral threshold by forming an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_alliance"] alliance with other parties, in which it is
sufficient that the total votes of the alliance passes 7%. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Independent_politician"] Independent candidates are not subject to an
electoral threshold.
After World War II, Turkey operated under a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-party_period_of_the_Republic_of_Turkey"] multi-party system. On the right side of the Turkish
 political spectrum, parties like [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Turkey,_historical)"] Democrat Party (DP), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justice_Party_(Turkey)"] Justice Party (AP), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motherland_Party_(Turkey)"] Motherland Party (ANAP)
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justice_and_Development_Party_(Turkey)"] Justice and Development Party (AKP) once became the largest political party in Turkey. Turkish 
 Recep Tayyip Erdoğan
 President
 right-wing parties are more likely to embrace principles of political ideologies such as conservatism,
 nationalism or Islamism.[171] On the left side of the spectrum, parties like Republican People's Party (CHP), Social Democratic
Populist Party (SHP) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Left_Party_(Turkey)"] Democratic Left Party (DSP) once enjoyed the largest electoral success. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left-wing_politics"] Left-wing parties are more likely
to embrace principles of socialism, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kemalism"] Kemalism or secularism.[172]
The 12th [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Turkey"] President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan"] Recep Tayyip Erdoğan, the winner of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_Turkish_presidential_election"] 2018 presidential election and former [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Turkey"] prime minister, is currently
serving as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_state"] head of state and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_government"] head of government. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kemal_K%C4%B1l%C4%B1%C3%A7daro%C4%9Flu"] Kemal Kılıçdaroğlu is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_main_opposition_leaders_of_Turkey"] main opposition leader of Turkey. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_%C5%9Eentop"] Mustafa Şentop
is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speaker_of_the_Grand_National_Assembly"] Speaker of the Grand National Assembly.
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/27th_Parliament_of_Turkey"] 27th Parliament of Turkey was installed following the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_Turkish_parliamentary_election"] 2018 parliamentary election, with the starting composition of 295 seats
 for the Justice and Development Party (AKP), 146 seats for the Republican People's Party (CHP), 67 seats for the Peoples'
Democratic Party (HDP), 49 seats for the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalist_Movement_Party"] Nationalist Movement Party (MHP) and 49 seats for the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_Party"] Good Party (İP).[173] The next
parliamentary election is scheduled to take place in 2023.
Law
 With the founding of the Republic, Turkey adopted a civil law legal system, replacing Sharia-derived Ottoman law. The Civil
Code, adopted in 1926, was based on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swiss_Civil_Code"] Swiss Civil Code of 1907 and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swiss_Code_of_Obligations"] Swiss Code of Obligations of 1911. Although it
underwent a number of changes in 2002, it retains much of the basis of the original Code. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criminal_Code"] Criminal Code, originally based on
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_law_codes#Penal_Code"] Italian Criminal Code, was replaced in 2005 by a Code with principles similar to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Penal_Code"] German Penal Code and German law
Page 11
generally. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Administrative_law"] Administrative law is based on the French equivalent and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procedural_law"] procedural law
generally shows the influence of the Swiss, German and French legal systems.[174]
Islamic principles do not play a part in the legal system.[175]
Turkey has adopted the principle of the separation of powers. In line with this principle,
judicial power is exercised by independent courts on behalf of the Turkish nation. The
independence and organisation of the courts, the security of the tenure of judges and
public prosecutors, the profession of judges and prosecutors, the supervision of judges
and public prosecutors, the military courts and their organisation, and the powers and
duties of the high courts are regulated by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Constitution"] Turkish Constitution.[176]  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul_%C3%87a%C4%9Flayan_Justice_Palace"] Istanbul Çağlayan Justice Palace is a
courthouse in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%9Ei%C5%9Fli"] Şişli district of
According to Article 142 of the Turkish Constitution, the organisation, duties and Istanbul.
jurisdiction of the courts, their functions and the trial procedures are regulated by law. In
line with the aforementioned article of the Turkish Constitution and related laws, the
court system in Turkey can be classified under three main categories; which are the Judicial Courts, Administrative Courts, and
Military Courts. Each category includes first instance courts and high courts. In addition, the Court of Jurisdictional Disputes rules
on cases that cannot be classified readily as falling within the purview of one court system.[176]
 Law enforcement in Turkey is carried out by several agencies under the jurisdiction of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_the_Interior_(Turkey)"] Ministry of Internal Affairs. These
agencies are the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Directorate_of_Security_(Turkey)"] General Directorate of Security, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gendarmerie_General_Command"] Gendarmerie General Command and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coast_Guard_Command_(Turkey)"] Coast Guard Command.
Furthermore, there are other law enforcement agencies with specific ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Intelligence_Organization_(Turkey)"] National Intelligence Organization, General Directorate of
Customs Protection, etc.) or local (Village guards, Municipal Police, etc.) assignments that are under the jurisdiction of the president
or different ministries.
In the years of government by the AKP and Erdoğan, particularly since 2013, the independence and integrity of the Turkish
judiciary has increasingly been said to be in doubt by institutions, parliamentarians and journalists both within and outside of
Turkey; due to political interference in the promotion of judges and prosecutors, and in their pursuit of public
duty.[177][178][179][180] The Turkey 2015 report of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Commission"] European Commission stated that "the independence of the judiciary and
respect of the principle of separation of powers have been undermined and judges and prosecutors have been under strong political
pressure."[177]
Foreign relations
Turkey is a founding member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey_and_the_United_Nations"] United Nations (1945),[181] the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD"] OECD (1961),[182]
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation"] OIC (1969),[183] the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe"] OSCE (1973),[184] the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_Cooperation_Organization"] ECO (1985),[185] the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organization_of_the_Black_Sea_Economic_Cooperation"] BSEC (1992),[186]
 the D-8 (1997)[187] and the G20 (1999).[188] Turkey was a member of the United Nations
Security Council in 1951–1952, 1954–1955, 1961 and 2009–2010.[189] In 2012 Turkey
became a dialogue partner of the SCO, and in 2013 became a member of the
ACD.[190][191]
In line with its traditional Western orientation, relations with Europe have always been a
central part of Turkish foreign policy. Turkey became [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_states_of_the_Council_of_Europe"] one of the early members of the
Council of Europe in 1950, applied for associate membership of the EEC (predecessor of
the European Union) in 1959 and became an associate member in 1963. After decades of
political negotiations, Turkey applied for full membership of the EEC in 1987, became an
associate member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_European_Union"] Western European Union in 1992, joined the EU Customs Union
in 1995 and has been in formal accession negotiations with the EU since 2005.[149][150] 
 After becoming one of the early
members of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Europe"] Council of Europe in
 1950, Turkey became an associate
member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Economic_Community"] EEC in 1963, joined
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union"] EU Customs Union in 1995 and
Turkey's support for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Cyprus"] Northern Cyprus in the Cyprus dispute complicates Turkey's relations
with the EU and remains a major stumbling block to the country's EU accession bid.[192] 
started [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accession_of_Turkey_to_the_European_Union"] full membership negotiations
with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union"] European Union in
The other defining aspect of Turkey's foreign policy was the country's long-standing 
2005.[149][150]
strategic alliance with the United States.[193][194] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truman_Doctrine"] Truman Doctrine in 1947 enunciated
 American intentions to guarantee the security of Turkey and Greece during the Cold War, and resulted in large-scale U.S. military
and economic support. In 1948 both countries were included in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshall_Plan"] Marshall Plan and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organisation_for_European_Economic_Co-operation"] OEEC for rebuilding European
economies.[195] The common threat posed by the Soviet Union during the Cold War led to Turkey's membership of NATO in
1952, ensuring close bilateral relations with the US. Subsequently, Turkey benefited from the United States' political, economic and
diplomatic support, including in key issues such as the country's bid to join the European Union.[196] In the post–Cold War
environment, Turkey's geostrategic importance shifted towards its proximity to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_East"] Middle East, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus"] Caucasus and the Balkans.[197]
The independence of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkic_states"] Turkic states of the Soviet Union in 1991, with which Turkey shares a common cultural and linguistic
heritage, allowed Turkey to extend its economic and political relations deep into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia"] Central Asia,[199] thus enabling the completion of
a multi-billion-dollar oil and natural gas [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baku%E2%80%93Tbilisi%E2%80%93Ceyhan_pipeline"] pipeline from Baku in Azerbaijan to the port of Ceyhan in Turkey. The Baku–Tbilisi–
Page 12
 Ceyhan pipeline forms part of Turkey's foreign policy strategy to become an energy conduit
from the Caspian Sea basin to Europe. However, in 1993, Turkey sealed its land border
with Armenia in a gesture of support to Azerbaijan (a Turkic state in the Caucasus region)
during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Nagorno-Karabakh_War"] First Nagorno-Karabakh War, and it remains closed.[200] Armenia and Turkey
started diplomatic talks in order to normalise the relationship between the two countries.
The discussions include opening the closed borders and starting trade. Turkey and Armenia
have also restarted commercial flights between the two countries.[201]The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Armed_Forces"] Turkish Armed Forces
collectively rank as the second-
largest standing military force in
NATO, after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces"] US Armed Forces.
Turkey joined the alliance in
1952.[198] 
Under the AKP government, Turkey's influence has grown in the formerly Ottoman
territories of the Middle East and the Balkans, based on the "strategic depth" doctrine (a
terminology that was coined by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmet_Davuto%C4%9Flu"] Ahmet Davutoğlu for defining Turkey's increased
engagement in regional foreign policy issues),  also called [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Ottomanism"] Neo-Ottomanism.[202][203]
Following the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Spring"] Arab Spring in December 2010, the choices made by the AKP government
for supporting certain political opposition groups in the affected countries have led to
tensions with some Arab states, such as Turkey's neighbour Syria since the start of the
 Syrian civil war, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt"] Egypt after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013_Egyptian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat"] ousting of President Mohamed Morsi.[204][205]
As of 2021, Turkey does not have an ambassador in either Syria or Egypt.[206] Diplomatic
relations with Israel were also severed after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_flotilla_raid"] Gaza flotilla raid in 2010, but were
normalised following a deal in June 2016.[207] These political rifts have left Turkey with
few allies in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levant"] East Mediterranean, where rich [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_gas"] natural gas fields have recently been
discovered;[208][209] in sharp contrast with the original goals that were set by the former
Foreign Minister (later Prime Minister) Ahmet Davutoğlu in his "zero problems with
neighbours"[210][211] foreign policy doctrine.[212] In 2015, Turkey, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia"] Saudi Arabia and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar"] Qatar
formed a "strategic alliance" against Syrian President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad"] Bashar al-Assad.[213] However,
following the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia%E2%80%93Turkey_relations#Normalisation_of_ties"] rapprochement with Russia in 2016, Turkey revised its stance regarding the
solution of the conflict in Syria.[214][215][216] In January 2018, the Turkish military and the 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_G20_Antalya_summit"] 2015 G20 Summit held in
Antalya, Turkey, a founding member
of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD"] OECD (1961) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G20"] G20 (1999).
Turkish-backed forces, including the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish-backed_Free_Syrian_Army"] Free Syrian Army and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahrar_al-Sham"] Ahrar al-Sham,[217] began an
 intervention in Syria aimed at ousting U.S.-backed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Protection_Units"] YPG from the enclave of
Afrin.[218][219] There is a dispute over Turkey's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aegean_dispute"] maritime boundaries with Greece and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus%E2%80%93Turkey_maritime_zones_dispute"] Cyprus and drilling rights in the eastern
Mediterranean.[220][221]
Military
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Armed_Forces"] Turkish Armed Forces consist of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Staff_of_the_Turkish_Armed_Forces"] General Staff, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Land_Forces"] Land Forces, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Naval_Forces"] Naval Forces
and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Air_Force"] Air Force. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_of_the_Turkish_General_Staff"] Chief of the General Staff is appointed by the President. President is
responsible to the Parliament for matters of national security and the adequate preparation
of the armed forces to defend the country. However, the authority to declare war and to
deploy the Turkish Armed Forces to foreign countries or to allow foreign armed forces to
be stationed in Turkey rests solely with the Parliament.[222]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Gendarmerie"] Gendarmerie General Command and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Coast_Guard"] Coast Guard Command are law enforcement
agencies with military organization (ranks, structure, etc.) and under the jurisdiction of the
 Ministry of the Interior. In wartime, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Turkey"] president can order certain units of the Gendarmerie
General Command and the Coast Guard Command to operate under the Land Forces
Command and Naval Forces Commands respectively. The remaining parts of the
Gendarmerie and the Coast Guard continue to carry out their law enforcement missions
under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Interior. 
 TAI Anka and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayraktar_TB2"] Bayraktar TB2 are the
unmanned aerial vehicles (UAV)
used by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Armed_Forces"] Turkish Armed Forces.
Every fit male Turkish citizen otherwise not barred is required to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscription_in_Turkey"] serve in the military for a
period ranging from three weeks to a year, dependent on education and job location.[223]
Turkey does not recognise [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscientious_objector"] conscientious objection and does not offer a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alternative_civilian_service"] civilian alternative
to military service.[224]  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TCG_Anadolu"] TCG Anadolu (L-400) is an
amphibious assault ship-aircraft
Turkey has the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_states_of_NATO#Military_personnel"] second-largest standing military force in NATO, after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces"] United States,
with an estimated strength of 890,700 military as of February 2022.[225] Turkey is one of 
 carrier developed for the Turkish
Navy
five NATO member states which are part of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_sharing"] nuclear sharing policy of the alliance,
 together with Belgium, Germany, Italy, and the Netherlands.[226] A total of 90 B61 nuclear
bombs are hosted at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incirlik_Air_Base"] Incirlik Air Base, 40 of which are allocated for use by the Turkish Air Force in case of a nuclear conflict,
but their use requires the approval of NATO.[227]
Page 13
Turkey has participated in international missions under the United Nations and NATO [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Brigade"] since the Korean War, including
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peacekeeping"] peacekeeping missions in Somalia, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Protection_Force"] Yugoslavia and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Ocean_Shield"] Horn of Africa. It supported [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coalition_of_the_Gulf_War"] coalition forces in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Gulf_War"] First Gulf War,
contributed military personnel to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force"] International Security Assistance Force in Afghanistan, and remains active in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosovo_Force"] Kosovo Force,
 Eurocorps and EU Battlegroups.[228][229] In recent years, Turkey has assisted Peshmerga forces in northern Iraq and the Somali
Armed Forces with security and training.[230][231] Turkish Armed Forces have a relatively substantial military presence
abroad,[232] with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_with_overseas_military_bases"] military bases in Albania,[233] Iraq,[234] Qatar,[235] and Somalia.[236] The country also maintains a force of
 36,000 troops in Northern Cyprus since 1974.[237]
Human rights
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_Turkey"] human rights record of Turkey has been the subject of much controversy and
international condemnation. Between 1959 and 2011 the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights"] European Court of Human Rights
made more than 2400 judgements against Turkey for human rights violations on issues such
as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_of_Kurdish_people_in_Turkey"] Kurdish rights, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Turkey"] women's rights, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Turkey"] LGBT rights, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_of_Turkey"] media freedom.[238][239] Turkey's
 human rights record continues to be a significant obstacle to the country's membership of
the EU.[240]
In the latter half of the 1970s, Turkey suffered from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_violence_in_Turkey_(1976%E2%80%931980)"] political violence between [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far-left_politics"] far-left and
 far-right militant groups, which culminated in the military coup of 1980.[241] The Kurdistan
Workers' Party - a.k.a. PKK - (designated a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_designated_terrorist_groups"] terrorist organisation by Turkey, the United 
Feminist demonstration in Kadıköy,
Istanbul on 29 July 2017
States,[141] the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union"] European Union[142] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organization"] NATO[242]) was founded in 1978 by a group of
Kurdish militants led by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_%C3%96calan"] Abdullah Öcalan, seeking the foundation of an independent Kurdish state based on [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_state"] Marxist-Leninist
ideology.[243] The initial reason given by the PKK for this was the oppression of Kurds in Turkey.[244][245] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdish%E2%80%93Turkish_conflict_(1978%E2%80%93present)"] A full-scale insurgency
began in 1984, when the PKK announced a Kurdish uprising. Following the arrest and imprisonment of Abdullah Öcalan in
1999,[146][147] the PKK modified its demands into equal rights for ethnic Kurds and provincial autonomy within
Turkey.[246][247][248][249] Since the conflict began, more than 40,000 people have died, most of whom were Turkish Kurds.[250]
The European Court of Human Rights and other international human rights organisations have condemned Turkey for human
rights abuses.[238][239] Many judgments are related to cases such as civilian deaths in aerial bombardments,[251] torturing,[252]
forced displacements,[253] destroyed villages,[254][255][256] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arbitrary_arrest"] arbitrary arrests,[257] murdered and disappeared Kurdish journalists,
activists and politicians.[258]
On 20 May 2016, the Turkish parliament stripped almost a quarter of its members of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_immunity"] immunity from prosecution, including 101
deputies from the pro-Kurdish [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peoples%27_Democratic_Party_(Turkey)"] HDP and the main opposition [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_People%27s_Party_(Turkey)"] CHP party.[259] In reaction to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_Turkish_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt"] failed coup attempt on 15 July
2016, over 160,000 judges, teachers, police and civil servants have been suspended or dismissed, 77,000 have been formally
arrested,[260][261] and 130 media organisations, including 16 television broadcasters and 45 newspapers,[262] have been closed by
the government of Turkey.[263] 160 journalists have been imprisoned.[264]
According to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_to_Protect_Journalists"] Committee to Protect Journalists, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justice_and_Development_Party_(Turkey)"] AKP government has waged one of
the world's biggest crackdowns on [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_freedom_in_Turkey"] media freedom.[265][266] Many journalists have been
arrested using charges of "terrorism" and "anti-state activities" such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ergenekon_(organization)"] Ergenekon and
 Balyoz cases, while thousands have been investigated on charges such as "denigrating
Turkishness" or "insulting Islam" in an effort to sow self-censorship.[265] In 2017, the CPJ
identified 81 jailed journalists in Turkey (including the editorial staff of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cumhuriyet"] Cumhuriyet,
Turkey's oldest newspaper still in circulation), all directly held for their published work (the
country ranked first in the world in that year, with more journalists in prison than in Iran,
Eritrea or China);[266] while in 2015 Freemuse identified nine musicians imprisoned for
their work (ranking third after Russia and China).[267] 
Turkish journalists protesting the
 imprisonment of their colleagues on
 Human Rights Day in 2016.
 During the October 2019 offensive into Syria, Turkish forces have been accused of war
crimes, such as targeting civilians with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_phosphorus"] white phosphorus and various other human rights violations.[268][269] Turkey has officially
rejected the claims.[270]
LGBT rights
 Homosexual activity is legal in Turkey.[272] However, LGBT people in Turkey face discrimination, harassment and even violence
from their relatives, neighbors, etc.[273] The Turkish authorities have carried out many discriminatory practices.[274][275][276]
Despite these, LGBT acceptance in Turkey is growing. In a survey conducted by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kadir_Has_University"] Kadir Has University in Istanbul in 2016, 33% of
respondents said that LGBT people should have equal rights, which increased to 45% in 2020. Another survey by Kadir Has
University in 2018 found that the proportion of people who would not want a homosexual neighbour decreased from 55% in 2018
to 47% in 2019.[277][278] A poll by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ipsos"] Ipsos in 2015 found that 27% of the Turkish public was in favor of legalizing same-sex
marriage and 19% supported [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_unions"] civil unions instead.[279]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Turkish_journalists_protesting_imprisonment_of_their_colleagues_in_2016.jpg"]
Page 14
 Istanbul Pride was held for the first time in 2003. Turkey became the first Muslim-majority
country to hold a gay pride march. It was also the first gay pride in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_East"] Middle East and the
Balkans.[280]
Geography 
Turkey is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transcontinental_country"] transcontinental country
 Topographic map of Turkey 
bridging [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeastern_Europe"] Southeastern Europe and
 Western Asia. Asian Turkey, which
includes 97 percent of the country's
 territory, is separated from European
 Turkey by the Bosphorus, the Sea of
Marmara, and the Dardanelles.
European Turkey comprises only 3
percent of the country's territory.[281]
Turkey covers an area of 783,562 square
kilometres (302,535 square miles),[282] 
 Istanbul Pride organized in 2003 for
the first time. Since 2015, parades in
 Istanbul were denied permission by
the government. The denials were
based on security concerns, but
critics claimed the bans were
ideological. Despite the refusal
hundreds of people defied the ban
each year.[271]
of which 755,688 square kilometres (291,773 square miles) is in Asia and 23,764 square
kilometres (9,175 square miles) is in Europe.[283] The country is encircled by seas on three sides: the Aegean Sea to the west, the
Black Sea to the north and the Mediterranean Sea to the south. Turkey also contains the Sea of Marmara in the northwest.[284]
 Turkey is divided into seven geographical regions: Marmara, Aegean, Black Sea, Central Anatolia, Eastern Anatolia, Southeastern
Anatolia and the Mediterranean. The uneven north Anatolian terrain running along the Black Sea resembles a long, narrow belt.
This region comprises approximately one-sixth of Turkey's total land area. As a general trend, the inland Anatolian plateau
becomes increasingly rugged as it progresses eastward.[284]Pamukkale terraces are made of travertine, a sedimentary rock
deposited by mineral water from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot_springs"] hot springs. The area is famous for a carbonate mineral left by the flowing of thermal spring
water.[285][286] It is located in Turkey's Inner Aegean region, in the River Menderes valley, which has a temperate climate for most
of the year. It was added as a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Turkey"] UNESCO World Heritage Site in 1988 with Hierapolis.
East Thrace; the European portion of Turkey, is located at the easternmost edge the
Balkans. It forms the border between Turkey and its neighbours Greece and Bulgaria. The
Asian part of the country mostly consists of the peninsula of Anatolia, which consists of a
high central plateau with narrow coastal plains, between the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C3%B6ro%C4%9Flu_Mountains"] Köroğlu and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pontic_Mountains"] Pontic mountain
ranges to the north and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taurus_Mountains"] Taurus Mountains to the south.
 The Eastern Anatolia Region mostly corresponds to the western part of the Armenian
 Highlands (the plateau situated between the Anatolian Plateau in the west and the Lesser
Caucasus in the north)[287] and contains [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Ararat"] Mount Ararat, Turkey's highest point at 5,137
metres (16,854 feet),[288] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake_Van"] Lake Van, the largest lake in the country.[289] Eastern
Turkey has a mountainous landscape and is home to the sources of rivers such as the
Euphrates, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tigris"] Tigris and Aras. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeastern_Anatolia_Region"] Southeastern Anatolia Region includes the northern
plains of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Mesopotamia"] Upper Mesopotamia. 
 Pamukkale
Far from the coast the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_of_Turkey"] climate of Turkey tends to be [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_climate"] continental but elsewhere temperate,
and has [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_Turkey"] become hotter, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malatya_Plain"] drier in parts. There are [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wildlife_of_Turkey"] many species of plants and animals.
Biodiversity 
 Cappadocia
Turkey's extraordinary [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecosystem"] ecosystem and habitat diversity has produced considerable species diversity.[290] Anatolia is the homeland
of many plants that have been cultivated for food since the advent of agriculture, and the wild ancestors of many plants that now
provide staples for humankind still grow in Turkey. The diversity of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fauna_of_Turkey"] Turkey's fauna is even greater than that of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flora_and_vegetation_of_Turkey"] its flora. The
number of animal species in the whole of Europe is around 60,000, while in Turkey there are over 80,000 (over 100,000 counting
the subspecies).[291]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Anatolian_conifer_and_deciduous_forests"] Northern Anatolian conifer and deciduous forests is an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecoregion"] ecoregion which covers most of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pontic_Mountains"] Pontic Mountains in northern
Turkey, while the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus_mixed_forests"] Caucasus mixed forests extend across the eastern end of the range. The region is home to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasia"] Eurasian wildlife such
as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasian_sparrowhawk"] Eurasian sparrowhawk, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_eagle"] golden eagle, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_imperial_eagle"] eastern imperial eagle, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lesser_spotted_eagle"] lesser spotted eagle, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasian_black_grouse"] Caucasian black grouse, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red-fronted_serin"] red-fronted serin,
 and wallcreeper.[292] The narrow coastal strip between the Pontic Mountains and the Black Sea is home to the Euxine-Colchic
deciduous forests, which contain some of the world's few [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperate_rainforest"] temperate rainforests.[293] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinus_brutia"] Turkish pine (Pinus brutia) is mostly
found in Turkey and other east Mediterranean countries; the other commonly found species of the genus [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pine"] Pinus (pine) in Turkey
include the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinus_nigra"] nigra, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinus_sylvestris"] sylvestris, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinus_pinea"] pinea and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinus_halepensis"] halepensis. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quercus_cerris"] Turkey oak (Quercus cerris) and numerous other species of the genus
Page 15
 Quercus (oak) exist in Turkey. The most commonly found species of the genus Platanus
(plane) is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Platanus_orientalis"] orientalis. Several wild species of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tulip"] tulip are native to Anatolia, and the flower
was first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tulip#Introduction_to_Western_Europe"] introduced to Western Europe with species taken from the Ottoman Empire in the
16th century.[294][295]
There are [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Turkey"] 40 national parks, 189 nature parks, 31
nature preserve areas, 80 wildlife protection areas and
 109 nature monuments in Turkey such as Gallipoli
 Peninsula Historical National Park, Mount Nemrut
 Sumela Monastery in the Pontic
Mountains, which form an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecoregion"] ecoregion
 with diverse temperate rainforest
types, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flora"] flora and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fauna"] fauna in northern 
 National Park, Ancient Troy National Park, Ölüdeniz
Nature Park and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polonezk%C3%B6y_Nature_Park"] Polonezköy Nature Park.[296] In the
21st century, threats to biodiversity include
 desertification due to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_Turkey"] climate change in Turkey.[297]
Anatolia. 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolian_leopard"] Anatolian leopard is still found in very small
numbers in the northeastern and southeastern regions
of Turkey.[298][299] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasian_lynx"] Eurasian lynx and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_wildcat"] European wildcat are other [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felidae"] felid species which
are currently found in the forests of Turkey. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_tiger"] Caspian tiger, now extinct, lived in the
easternmost regions of Turkey until the latter half of the 20th century.[298][300] 
A white [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Angora"] Turkish Angora cat with
 odd eyes (heterochromia), which
is common among the Angoras.
Renowned domestic animals from Ankara, the capital of Turkey, include the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Angora"] Angora cat,
 Angora rabbit and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angora_goat"] Angora goat; and from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Van_Province"] Van Province the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Van"] Van cat. The national dog breeds are the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kangal_Shepherd_Dog"] Kangal ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolian_Shepherd"] Anatolian Shepherd),
 Malaklı and Akbaş.[301]
Climate 
The coastal areas of Turkey bordering the Aegean and Mediterranean Seas have
a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperate"] temperate [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_climate"] Mediterranean climate, with hot, dry summers and mild to cool, wet
winters.[302] The coastal areas bordering the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Sea"] Black Sea have a temperate
 oceanic climate with warm, wet summers and cool to cold, wet winters.[302]
The Turkish Black Sea coast receives the most [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)"] precipitation and is the only
region of Turkey that receives high precipitation throughout the year.[302] The
 Köppen climate classification of Turkey 
eastern part of the Black Sea coast averages 2,200 millimetres (87 in) annually
which is the highest precipitation in the country.[302] The coastal areas bordering
the Sea of Marmara, which connects the Aegean Sea and the Black Sea, have a
transitional climate between a temperate Mediterranean climate and a temperate
oceanic climate with warm to hot, moderately dry [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Summer"] summers and cool to cold, wet winters.[302] Snow falls on the coastal areas of the
Sea of Marmara and the Black Sea almost every winter, but usually melts in no more than a few days.[302] However, snow is rare
in the coastal areas of the Aegean Sea and very rare in the coastal areas of the Mediterranean Sea.[302] Winters on the Anatolian
plateau are especially severe. Temperatures of −30 °C to −40 °C (−22 °F to −40 °F) do occur in northeastern Anatolia, and snow
may lie on the ground for at least 120 days of the year, and during the entire year on the summits of the highest mountains. In
central Anatolia the temperatures can drop below −20 °C ( -4 °F) with the mountains being even colder.
Mountains close to the coast prevent Mediterranean influences from extending inland, giving the central Anatolian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plateau"] plateau of the
interior of Turkey a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_climate"] continental climate with sharply contrasting seasons.[302]
Economy
Turkey is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newly_industrialized_country"] newly industrialized country, with an upper-middle income economy, which is
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)"] twentieth-largest in the world by nominal GDP, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)"] eleventh-largest by PPP.
Turkey is one of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emerging_7"] Emerging 7 countries. According to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank"] World Bank estimates, Turkey's
GDP per capita by PPP is $32,278 in 2021,[8] and approximately 11.7% of Turks are at risk
of poverty or social exclusion as of 2019.[303] Unemployment in Turkey was 13.6% in
2019,[304] and the middle class population in Turkey rose from 18% to 41% of the
population between 1993 and 2010 according to the World Bank.[305] As of
September 2021, the foreign currency reserves of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Bank_of_the_Republic_of_Turkey"] Turkish Central Bank were $74.9
billion (an 8.1% increase compared to the previous month), its gold reserves were $38.5 
 Istanbul is the largest city and
financial centre of Turkey.
billion (a 5.1% decrease compared to the previous month), while its official reserve assets
stood at $121.3 billion.[306] As of October 2021, the foreign currency deposits of the citizens and residents in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_banks_in_Turkey"] Turkish banks stood
at $234 billion, equivalent to around half of all deposits.[307][308] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union_%E2%80%93_Turkey_Customs_Union"] EU–Turkey Customs Union in 1995 led to an extensive
liberalisation of tariff rates, and forms one of the most important pillars of Turkey's foreign trade policy.[309]
Page 16
 The automotive industry in Turkey is sizeable, and produced over 1.3 million motor vehicles in 2015, ranking as the 14th largest
producer in the world.[310] Turkish automotive companies like TEMSA, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otokar"] Otokar and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BMC_(Turkey)"] BMC are among the world's largest van, bus
and truck manufacturers. Turkish [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shipyard"] shipyards are highly regarded both for the production of chemical and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oil_tanker"] oil tankers up to 10,000
 dwt and also for their mega yachts.[311] Turkish brands like Beko and Vestel are among the largest producers of consumer
electronics and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Home_appliances"] home appliances in Europe, and invest a substantial amount of funds for research and development in new
technologies related to these fields.[312][313][314]
Other key sectors of the Turkish economy are banking, construction, home
appliances, electronics, textiles, oil refining, petrochemical products, food,
mining, iron and steel, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_industry"] machine industry. In 2004, it was estimated that
46 percent of total disposable income was received by the top 20 percent of
income earners, while the lowest 20 percent received only 6 percent.[315]
 Foreign direct investment (FDI) in Turkey reached 22.05 billion USD in
2007 and 19.26 billion USD in 2015, but has declined in recent years.[316] In
the economic crisis of 2016 it emerged that the huge debts incurred for
investment during the AKP government since 2002 had mostly been
consumed in construction, rather than invested in sustainable economic
growth.[317] In 2020, according to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_Tracker"] Carbon Tracker, money was being wasted
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Energy_Agency"] constructing more coal-fired power stations in Turkey.[318] International
Energy Agency said that [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_subsidy#Turkey"] fossil fuel subsidies should be redirected, for 
A proportional representation of Turkey's exports,
2019
example to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_in_Turkey"] health system.[319] Fossil fuel subsidies were around 0.2% of
GDP for the first two decades of the 21st century,[320][321] and are higher than clean [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_subsidies"] energy subsidies.[322] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/External_costs"] external costs of
 fossil fuel consumption in 2018 has been estimated as 1.5% of GDP.[323] In 2020 the European Bank for Reconstruction and
Development offered to support a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Just_transition"] just transition away from coal.[324]
Turkey has seen a growth in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_gaming_industry"] video gaming industry during the recent years. Many game developing companies founded and gained
investment from venture capitalists. [325] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TaleWorlds_Entertainment"] TaleWorlds Entertainment, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peak_Games"] Peak Games, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bigger_Games&action=edit&redlink=1"] Bigger Games and Dream Games are the current
leaders in this sector. [326] [327]
Tourism
 Tourism in Turkey has increased almost every year in the 21st century,[328]
 and is an important part of the economy. The Turkish Ministry of Culture and
Tourism currently promotes Turkish tourism under the project [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey_Home"] Turkey Home.
Turkey is one of the world's top ten destination countries, with the highest
percentage of foreign visitors arriving from Europe; specially Germany and
Russia in recent years.[328] In 2019, Turkey [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Tourism_rankings#Most_visited_destinations_by_international_tourist_arrivals"] ranked sixth in the world in
terms of the number of international tourist arrivals behind Italy, with 51.2
 million foreign tourists visiting the country.[329] Turkey has 19 UNESCO [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marmaris"] Marmaris in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Riviera"] Turkish Riviera
World Heritage Sites, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Turkey_(Tentative_list)"] 84 World Heritage Sites in tentative list. Turkey is
home to 519 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Flag_beaches"] Blue Flag beaches, which makes it in the third place in the
world.[330] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul"] Istanbul is the tenth most visited city in the world with 13,433,000 annual visitors as of 2018.[331] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antalya"] Antalya is the second
most visited city in Turkey, with over 9 million tourists in 2021. [332]
Infrastructure
In 2013 there were 98 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Turkey"] airports in Turkey,[334] including 22 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_airport"] international airports.[335]
 İstanbul Airport is planned to be the largest airport in the world, with a capacity to serve
150 million passengers a year.[336][337] As well as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Airlines"] Turkish Airlines, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_carrier"] flag carrier of Turkey
since 1933, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_airlines_of_Turkey"] several other airlines operate in the country. It operates scheduled services to
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainline_(aeronautics)"] 315 destinations in Europe, Asia, Africa, and the Americas, making it the largest mainline
carrier in the world by number of passenger destinations.[338][339][340] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Airlines"] Turkish Airlines
uses [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul_Airport"] Istanbul Airport of 90 million capacity as its main hub.
As of 2014, the country has a roadway network of over 65,000 kilometres (40,400
miles).[341] Motorways are controlled-access highways that are officially named Otoyol.
The network spans 3,523 kilometres (2,189 mi) as of 2020. The network is expected to
expand to 4,773 kilometres (2,966 mi) by 2023 and to 9,312 kilometres (5,786 mi) by
2035. [342] 
 Istanbul Airport main terminal
building has an annual passenger
capacity of 90 million and making it
the world's largest [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airport_terminal"] airport terminal
building under a single roof.[333]
Page 17
 Turkish State Railways operates both conventional and high speed trains on 12,532 kilometres rail length. The government-owned
national railway company started building [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Turkey"] high-speed rail lines in 2003. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara-Konya_high-speed_railway"] Ankara-Konya line became operational in 2011, while
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara-Istanbul_high-speed_railway"] Ankara-Istanbul line entered service in 2014.[343] Konya-Karaman line started its operations in 2022 and 406 km (252 mi) long
 Ankara-Sivas line is to open in 2022.
Opened in 2013, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marmaray"] Marmaray tunnel under the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosphorus"] Bosphorus connects the railway and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul_Metro"] metro lines of Istanbul's European and Asian
sides; while the nearby [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasia_Tunnel"] Eurasia Tunnel (2016) provides an undersea road connection for motor vehicles.[344]
 Metro Istanbul is the largest metro network in the country with 495 million annual ridership.[345] There are 8 metro lines under
service and 5 more under construction.[346]
 The Bosphorus Bridge (1973), Fatih Sultan Mehmet Bridge (1988) and Yavuz Sultan
Selim Bridge (2016) are the three suspension bridges connecting the European and Asian
shores of the Bosphorus strait. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_Gazi_Bridge"] Osman Gazi Bridge (2016) connects the northern and
southern shores of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_%C4%B0zmit"] Gulf of İzmit. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%87anakkale_1915_Bridge"] Çanakkale 1915 Bridge on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dardanelles"] Dardanelles strait,
connecting Europe and Asia, is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_longest_suspension_bridge_spans#Bridges_under_construction"] longest suspension bridge in the world.[348]
Many [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_gas_in_Turkey"] natural gas pipelines span the country's territory.[161] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Stream"] Blue Stream, a major trans-
 Black Sea gas pipeline, delivers natural gas from Russia to Turkey. The undersea pipeline,
 Turkish Stream, with an annual capacity around 63 billion cubic metres (2,200 billion cubic
 feet), allows Turkey to resell Russian gas to the rest of Europe.[349] The Baku-Tbilisi-
Ceyhan pipeline, the second longest [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oil_pipeline"] oil pipeline in the world, was inaugurated in 2005.[350] 
A [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TCDD_HT80000"] TCDD HT80000 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Turkey"] high-speed train of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_State_Railways"] Turkish State Railways[347]
As of 2018 Turkey consumes 1700 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terawatt"] terawatt hours (TW/h) of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primary_energy"] primary energy per year, a
little over 20 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megawatt"] megawatt hours (MW/h) per person, mostly from imported [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fossil_fuels"] fossil fuels.[351] Although the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_policy_of_Turkey"] energy policy of Turkey
includes reducing fossil-fuel imports, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coal_in_Turkey"] coal in Turkey is the largest single reason why [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions_by_Turkey"] greenhouse gas emissions by Turkey amount
to 1% of the global total. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_Turkey"] Renewable energy in Turkey is being increased and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akkuyu_Nuclear_Power_Plant"] Akkuyu Nuclear Power Plant is being built on the
 Mediterranean coast: but despite [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electricity_sector_in_Turkey"] national electricity generation overcapacity [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fossil_fuel_subsidies"] fossil fuels are still subsidized.[352] Turkey has the
fifth-highest direct utilisation and capacity of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geothermal_power_in_Turkey"] geothermal power in the world.[353]
As of 2019, Turkey produces 45.6% of its electricity from renewable sources.[354]
Science and technology
 TÜBİTAK is the leading agency for developing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Turkey"] science, technology and innovation policies in Turkey.[355] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Academy_of_Sciences"] TÜBA is an
autonomous scholarly society acting to promote scientific activities in Turkey.[356] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TAEK"] TAEK is the country's official [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_technology"] nuclear energy
institution, focused on academic research and the development and implementation of peaceful nuclear technology.[357] It is
supervising the construction of Turkey's first nuclear facility, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akkuyu_Nuclear_Power_Plant"] Akkuyu Nuclear Power Plant in Mersin, at the cost of $20 billion; the
plant is expected to be operational in May 2023,[358] and is projected to meet around 10% of the country's electricity demand.
 The Turkish government invests heavily in research and development of military
technologies, including [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Aerospace_Industries"] Turkish Aerospace Industries, ASELSAN, HAVELSAN,
ROKETSAN, and MKE. Turkey is a global leader in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle"] unmanned aerial vehicles (UAV); the
 Bayraktar TB2, manufactured by private defence company Baykar, has been exported to
 over a dozen countries and played a decisive role in several conflicts, including the 2020
Nagorno-Karabakh war and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine"] 2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine.[359][360]
Turkey has made significant inroads in aerospace technology into the 21st century. In 2013,
it initiated the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Launch_System_(Turkey)"] Turkish Space Launch System (UFS) to develop an independent satellite
 launch capability, including the construction of a spaceport, the development of satellite
launch vehicles, and the establishment of remote earth stations.[361][362][363] Türksat, the
country's sole [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communications_satellite"] communications satellite operator, has launched a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turksat_(satellite)"] series of satellites into
orbit; likewise, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Satellite_Assembly,_Integration_and_Test_Center"] Turkish Satellite Assembly, Integration and Test Center (UMET)—a
spacecraft production and testing facility owned by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Defence_(Turkey)"] Ministry of National Defence and
operated by the TAI—has launched the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6kt%C3%BCrk-1"] Göktürk series of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth_observation_satellite"] Earth observation satellites for
reconnaissance; [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BILSAT-1"] BILSAT-1 and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RASAT"] RASAT are the scientific Earth observation satellites
operated by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T%C3%9CB%C4%B0TAK_Space_Technologies_Research_Institute"] TÜBİTAK Space Technologies Research Institute. 
 Göktürk-1, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6kt%C3%BCrk-2"] Göktürk-2 and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6kt%C3%BCrk-3"] Göktürk-3
are the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth_observation_satellite"] Earth observation satellites
 of the Turkish Ministry of National
Defense, while state-owned [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T%C3%BCrksat_(company)"] Türksat
operates the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T%C3%BCrksat_(satellite)"] Türksat series of
 communications satellites.
In 2015, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aziz_Sancar"] Aziz Sancar, a Turkish professor at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina"] University of North Carolina, won the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Chemistry_Prize"] Nobel Prize in Chemistry for his work on
how cells repair damaged DNA;[364] he is one of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_country#Turkey"] two Turkish Nobel laureates, and the first in the sciences. Other prominent
Turkish scientists include physician [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hulusi_Beh%C3%A7et"] Hulusi Behçet, who discovered [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beh%C3%A7et%27s_disease"] Behçet's disease; mathematician [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cahit_Arf"] Cahit Arf, who defined the
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arf_invariant"] Arf invariant; and immunologists [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U%C4%9Fur_%C5%9Eahin"] Uğur Şahin and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%96zlem_T%C3%BCreci"] Özlem Türeci, whose German [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biotechnology"] biotechnology company, BioNTech, developed
 one of the first efficacious vaccines against [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19"] COVID-19.
Page 18
Turkey is among the top fifty most innovative countries in the world, ranking 41st in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index"] Global Innovation Index in 2021; this
represents a considerable increase since 2011, where it was ranked 65th.[365]
Demographics
 Total fertility rate in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependencies_by_total_fertility_rate"] Turkey by
 province (2021)[366]
    3–4
    2–3
    1.5-2
    1-1.5 
According to the Address-Based Population Recording System of Turkey, the country's
population was 74.7 million people in 2011,[368] nearly three-quarters of whom lived in
 towns and cities. According to the 2011 estimate, the population is increasing by 1.35
percent each year. Turkey has an average population density of 97 people per km². People
within the 15–64 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_group"] age group constitute 67.4 percent of the total population; the 0–14 age
group corresponds to 25.3 percent; while senior citizens aged 65 years or older make up 7.3
percent.[369]
Article 66 of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Constitution"] Turkish Constitution defines a "Turk" as "anyone who is bound to the
Turkish state through the bond of citizenship"; therefore, the legal use of the term "Turkish"
as a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Citizenship"] citizen of Turkey is different from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_group"] ethnic definition.[370] However approximately
70 to 80 percent of the country's citizens are ethnic Turks.[371][4] It is estimated that there
are at least 47 ethnic groups represented in Turkey.[372] Reliable data on the ethnic mix of
the population is not available, because Turkish census figures do not include statistics on
ethnicity.[373]
 Kurds are the largest non-Turkish ethnicity at anywhere from 12–25 per cent of the
population.[374][375] The exact figure remains a subject of dispute; according to Servet
Mutlu, "more often than not, these estimates reflect pro-Kurdish or pro-Turkish sympathies
 CIA map of areas with a Kurdish and attitudes rather than scientific facts or erudition".[372] Mutlu's 1990 study estimated
majority[367]  Kurds made up around 12 per cent of the population, while [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehrdad_Izady"] Mehrdad Izady placed the
figure around 25 per cent.[376] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurds"] Kurds make up a majority in the provinces of Ağrı,
Batman, Bingöl, Bitlis, Diyarbakır, Hakkari, Iğdır, Mardin, Muş, Siirt, Şırnak, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tunceli_Province"] Tunceli and
Van; a near majority in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%9Eanl%C4%B1urfa_Province"] Şanlıurfa Province (47%); and a large minority in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kars_Province"] Kars Province (20%).[377] In addition, due to internal
migration, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdish_diaspora"] Kurdish diaspora communities exist in all of the major cities in central and western Turkey. In Istanbul, there are an
estimated three million Kurds, making it the city with the largest Kurdish population in the world.[378] Non-Kurdish minorities are
believed to make up an estimated 7–12 percent of the population.[4]
The three "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Millet_(Ottoman_Empire)"] Non-Muslim" minority groups recognised in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Lausanne"] Treaty of Lausanne were Armenians, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greeks_in_Turkey"] Greeks and Jews. Other ethnic
groups include Albanians, Arabs, Assyrians, Bosniaks, Circassians, Georgians, Laz, Pomaks, and Roma.[4][379][380][381][382]
Turkey is also home to a Muslim community of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megleno-Romanians"] Megleno-Romanians.[383]
Before the start of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_civil_war"] Syrian civil war in 2011, the estimated number of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Turkey"] Arabs in Turkey varied from 1 million to more than 2
 million.[384] As of April 2020, there are 3.6 million Syrian refugees in Turkey, who are mostly Arabs but also include Syrian
Kurds, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_Turkmen"] Syrian Turkmen, and other [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Syria"] ethnic groups of Syria. The vast majority of these are living in Turkey with temporary residence
 permits. The Turkish government has granted Turkish citizenship to refugees who have joined the Syrian National
Army.[385][386][387]
