Immigration
Page 19
 Millions of Kurds fled across the mountains to Turkey and Kurdish areas of Iran during the Gulf War in 1991. Immigration to
Turkey is the process by which people [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_migration"] migrate to Turkey to reside in the country. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey%27s_migrant_crisis"] Turkey's migrant crisis created after an estimated
2.5 percent of the population are [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_migration"] international migrants.[388] Turkey hosts the largest number of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refugee"] refugees in the world, including 3.6
million [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_Civil_War_in_Turkey"] Syrian refugees, as of April 2020.[385] As part of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey%27s_migrant_crisis"] Turkey's migrant crisis, according to UNHCR, in 2018 Turkey was
hosting 63.4% of all the refugees in the world, that is 3,564,919 registered refugees from Africa and the Middle East in total.[389]
Languages
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Official_language"] official language is Turkish, which is the most widely spoken [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkic_languages"] Turkic language in the world.[390][391] It is spoken by 85.54
percent of the population as a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_language"] first language.[392] 11.97 percent of the population speaks the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurmanji"] Kurmanji dialect of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdish_languages"] Kurdish as their
mother tongue.[392] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language"] Arabic and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zaza_language"] Zaza are the mother tongues of 2.39 percent of the population, and several other languages are the
mother tongues of smaller parts of the population.[392] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endangered_language"] Endangered [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Languages_of_Turkey"] languages in Turkey include Abaza, Abkhaz, Adyghe,
 Cappadocian Greek, Gagauz, Hértevin, Homshetsma, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kabard-Cherkes"] Kabard-Cherkes, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaeo-Spanish"] Ladino (Judesmo), Laz, Mlahso, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pontic_Greek"] Pontic Greek, Romani,
Suret, Turoyo, Ubykh, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Armenian"] Western Armenian.[393] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megleno-Romanian_language"] Megleno-Romanian is also spoken.[383]
Religion 
Turkey is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secular_state"] secular state with no official [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_religion"] state religion; the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Constitution"] Turkish Constitution provides for
 freedom of religion and conscience.[394][395] A 2016 survey by Ipsos, interviewing 17,180
adults across 22 countries, found that [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam"] Islam was the dominant religion in Turkey, adhered to
by 82% of the total population; religiously unaffiliated people comprised 13% of the
population, while 2% were Christians.[396] According to a religiosity poll conducted in
Sancaklar Mosque is a contemporary
mosque in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul"] Istanbul 
Turkey in 2019 by OPTİMAR, 89.5% of the population identifies as Muslims, 4.5%
believed in God but did not belong to any organized religion, 2.7% were agnostics, 1.7%
were atheists, and 1.7% did not answer.[397][398] Another poll conducted by Gezici
Araştırma in 2020 interviewed 1,062 people in 12 provinces and found that 28.5% of the
 Generation Z in Turkey identify as irreligious.[399][400] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook"] CIA World Factbook reports that Islam is the religion of 99.8% of the
population, with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunni"] Sunni Muslims as the largest sect, while 0.2% are Christians and Jews.[401] However, there are no official
governmental statistics specifying the religious beliefs of the Turkish people, nor is religious data recorded in the country's
census.[402] Academics suggest the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alevi"] Alevi population may be from 15 to 20 million, while the Alevi-Bektaşi Federation states that
there are around 25 million.[403][404] According to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aksiyon"] Aksiyon magazine, the number of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twelver"] Twelver [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_Islam"] Shias (excluding Alevis) is three
million (4.2%).[405]
 Christianity has a long history in present-day Turkey, which is the birthplace of numerous
Christian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twelve_apostles"] apostles and saints. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antioch"] Antioch (Antakya) is regarded by tradition as the spot where
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gospels"] Gospels were written, and where the followers of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesus"] Jesus were called Christians for the
first time. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantinople"] Constantinople is generally considered to be the center and the "cradle of
Orthodox [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_civilization"] Christian civilization".[407][408] The percentage of Christians in Turkey fell from
17.5% (three million followers) in a population of 16 million to 2.5% percent in the early
 20th century.[409] mainly as a result of the Armenian genocide, the population exchange
between Greece and Turkey,[410] and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_emigration"] emigration of Christians that began in the late
19th century and gained pace in the first quarter of the 20th century.[411] Today, there are
more than 120,000–320,000 people of various [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_denominations"] Christian denominations,[412] representing
 less than 0.2% of Turkey's population,[413] including an estimated 80,000 Oriental
 Orthodox, 35,000 Roman Catholics,[414] 18,000 Antiochian Greeks,[415] 5,000 Greek
Orthodox, smaller numbers of Protestants,[416] and 512 Mormons.[417] Currently, there are
236 churches open for worship in Turkey.[418]
Modern-day Turkey continues to have a small Jewish population;[419] with around 26,000
 Jews, the vast majority of whom are Sephardi.[420] Turkey has the biggest Jewish
community among the Muslim-majority countries.[421][422] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Church_of_St._Anthony_of_Padua,_Istanbul"] Church of St. Anthony of Padua
on [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%B0stiklal_Avenue"] İstiklal Avenue, in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beyo%C4%9Flu"] Beyoğlu
district of Istanbul. There are 234
active churches in the city.[406]
In a mid-2010s poll, 2.9% of Turkish respondents identified as atheists.[423] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ateizm_Derne%C4%9Fi"] Association of Atheism, the first official atheist
organisation in the Balkans and the Middle East, was founded in 2014.[424][425] Some religious and secular officials have claimed
that [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atheism"] atheism and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deism"] deism are growing among Turkish people.[426][427][428][429]
Education
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suret"]
Page 20
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Education_(Turkey)"] Ministry of National Education is responsible for pre-tertiary education.[431] This is
compulsory and lasts twelve years: four years each of primary school, middle school and
high school.[432] All 12 years compulsory education is free of charge in public
schools.[433]
Basic education in Turkey is said to lag behind other OECD countries, with significant
differences between high and low performers.[434] Access to high-quality school heavily
 Istanbul Technical University is the
world's third-oldest technical 
depends on the performance in the secondary school entrance exams, to the point that some
students begin taking private tutoring classes when they are ten years old.[434]
university.[430] 
As of 2017, there are 190 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universities_in_Turkey"] universities in Turkey.[435] Except for the Open Education
Faculties (AÖF) at Anadolu, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul_University"] Istanbul and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk_University"] Atatürk University; entrance is regulated by the
national [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Student_Selection_and_Placement_System"] Student Selection and Placement System (ÖSYS) examination, after which high school graduates are assigned to
universities according to their performance.[436] According to the 2012–2013 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings"] Times Higher Education World University Rankings,
 the top university in Turkey is Middle East Technical University, followed by Bilkent University and Koç University, Istanbul
 Technical University and Boğaziçi University.[437] All state and private universities are under the control of the Higher Education
Board (YÖK), whose head is appointed by the President of Turkey; and since 2016 the President directly appoints all rectors of all
state and private universities.[438]
Turkey is a member of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socrates_programme"] Socrates programme, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erasmus_Programme"] Erasmus Programme and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erasmus%2B"] Erasmus+
Programmes. These student exchange programmes are organised by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union"] European Union.
[440] Also it is a member of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erasmus_Student_Network"] Erasmus Student Network which is a Europe-wide student
organisation which [441] has more than 15.000 volunteers across the Europe.
Turkey has become a hub for foreign students in recent years. The number of foreign
students in Turkey was 795.962 in 2016.[442] The government has announced a vision to
draw around 500,000 foreign students at its universities by offering attractive
scholarships.[443] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T%C3%BCrkiye_Scholarships"] Türkiye Scholarships is international scholarship program funded by
Government of Turkey. In 2021, in response to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T%C3%BCrkiye_Scholarships"] Türkiye Scholarships, that was advertised
in January 2021, Turkish Government received 165,000 applications from 178 countries of
the World.[444][445][446] 
 Istanbul University was founded in
1453 as a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_of_technology"] Darülfünûn. On 1 August
1933 it was reorganised and became
the Republic's first university.[439]
Health
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_(Turkey)"] Ministry of Health has run a universal public healthcare system since 2003.[447]
Known as Universal Health Insurance (Genel Sağlık Sigortası), it is funded by a tax
surcharge on employers, currently at 5%.[447] Public-sector funding covers approximately
75.2% of health expenditures.[447] Despite the universal health care, total expenditure on
health as a share of GDP in 2018 was the lowest among OECD countries at 6.3% of GDP,
compared to the OECD average of 9.3%.[447] The lower health care expenditure is due to
lower median age in Turkey which is 32.4, compared to Italy which is 47.3.[448] Aging
population is the prime reason for higher healthcare expenditure in the developed
world.[449] 
Acıbadem Hospital in Altunizade
neighborhood of Üsküdar, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%B0stanbul"] İstanbul
Average life expectancy is 78.6 years (75.9 for males and 81.3 for females), compared with
the EU average of 81 years.[447] Turkey has high rates of obesity, with 29.5% of its adult population having a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_mass_index"] body mass index
(BMI) value that is 30 or above.[450] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_pollution_in_Turkey"] Air pollution in Turkey is a major cause of early death.[451]
There are many private hospitals in the country. Turkey benefits from medical tourism in the recent years. Health tourism earns
above $1 billion to Turkey in 2019. Some 60% of the income is obtained from plastic surgery and a total of 662,087 patients
received service in the country last year within the scope of health tourism.[452]
Culture
Turkey has a very diverse culture that is a blend of various elements of the Turkic, Anatolian, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_the_Ottoman_Empire"] Ottoman (which was itself a
 continuation of both Greco-Roman and Islamic cultures) and Western culture and traditions, which started with the Westernisation
of the Ottoman Empire and still continues today.[453][454] This mix originally began as a result of the encounter of Turks and their
culture with those of the peoples who were in their path during [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkic_migration"] their migration from Central Asia to the West.[453][455] Turkish
culture is a product of efforts to be a "modern" Western state, while maintaining traditional religious and historical values.[453]
Page 21
Visual arts
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_miniature"] Ottoman miniature is linked to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_miniature"] Persian miniature tradition, as well as strong [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_painting#Late_imperial_China_(1368%E2%80%931895)"] Chinese
artistic influences. The words tasvir or nakış were used to define the art of miniature
painting in Ottoman Turkish. The studios the artists worked in were called
nakkaşhane.[456] The miniatures were usually not signed, perhaps because of the rejection
of individualism, but also because the works were not created entirely by one person; the
head painter designed the composition of the scene, and his apprentices drew the contours
(which were called tahrir) with black or colored ink and then painted the miniature without
creating an illusion of depth. The head painter, and much more often the scribe of the text,
were indeed named and depicted in some of the manuscripts. The understanding of
perspective was different from that of the nearby European Renaissance painting tradition,
and the scene depicted often included different time periods and spaces in one picture. They
followed closely the context of the book they were included in, more illustrations than
standalone works of art.[457] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matrak%C3%A7%C4%B1_Nasuh"] Matrakçı Nasuh (1480–1564) is one of the most prominent
artists of this era.  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ortak%C3%B6y_Mosque"] Ortaköy Mosque is a good example
of the Westernisation of Islamic-
 Turkish painting, in the Western sense, developed actively starting from the mid 19th
 century. The first painting lessons were scheduled at what is now the Istanbul Technical
University (then the Imperial Military Engineering School) in 1793, mostly for technical
purposes.[458] In the late 19th century, human figure in the Western sense was being 
 Ottoman architecture. Many [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baroque"] Baroque
architecture elements can be seen in
it.
established in Turkish painting, especially with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_Hamdi_Bey"] Osman Hamdi Bey (1842–1910).
Impressionism, among the contemporary trends, appeared later on with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halil_Pasha_(painter)"] Halil Pasha (c.1857–1939). Other important Turkish
painters in the 19th century were [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferik_%C4%B0brahim_Pasha"] Ferik İbrahim Paşa (1815–1891), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_Nuri_Pasha_(painter)"] Osman Nuri Paşa (c.1839–1906), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%9Eeker_Ahmet_Pa%C5%9Fa"] Şeker Ahmet Paşa (1841–
1907), and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hoca_Ali_Riza"] Hoca Ali Riza (1864–1939). 
The young Turkish artists sent to
Europe in 1926 came back inspired
by contemporary trends such as
Fauvism, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cubism"] Cubism and Expressionism,
still very influential in Europe. The
later "Group D" of artists led by
 Abidin Dino, Cemal Tollu, Fikret
 Mualla, Fahrünnisa Zeid, Bedri
Rahmi Eyüboğlu, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adnan_Coker"] Adnan Çoker and
 Burhan Doğançay introduced some
trends that had lasted in the West for
more than three decades.
16th century map of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matrak%C3%A7%C4%B1_Nasuh"] Matrakçı Nasuh (left) and Two Musician Girls of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_Hamdi_Bey"] Osman Hamdi Bey (right). 
Other important movements in
Turkish painting were the "Yeniler
Grubu" (The Newcomers Group) of
the late 1930s; the "On'lar Grubu" (Group of Ten) of the 1940s; the "Yeni Dal Grubu" (New Branch Group) of the 1950s; and the
"Siyah Kalem Grubu" (Black Pen Group) of the 1960s.[459]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuzgun_Acar"] Internationally acclaimed Turkish sculptors in the 20th century include Ali Hadi Bara, Zühtü Müridoğlu, İlhan Koman, Kuzgun
Acar and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Teoman_Germaner"] Ali Teoman Germaner.
 Carpet (halı) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kilim"] tapestry (kilim) [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weaving"] weaving is a traditional Turkish art form with roots in pre-Islamic times. During its long history,
the art and craft of weaving carpets and tapestries in Turkey has integrated numerous cultural traditions. Apart from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkic_peoples"] Turkic
design patterns that are prevalent, traces of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_carpet"] Persian and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_silk#Tapestry_and_embroidery"] Byzantine patterns can also be detected. There are also similarities with the
patterns used in Armenian, Caucasian and Kurdish carpet designs. The arrival of Islam in Central Asia and the development of
 Islamic art also influenced Turkic patterns in the medieval period. The history of the designs, motifs and ornaments used in Turkish
carpets and tapestries thus reflects the political and ethnic history of the Turks and the cultural diversity of Anatolia. However,
scientific attempts were unsuccessful, as yet, to attribute a particular design to a specific ethnic, regional, or even nomadic versus
village tradition.[460]
The earliest examples of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_paper_marbling"] Turkish paper marbling, called [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paper_marbling"] ebru in Turkish, are said to be a copy of the Hâlnâme by the poet Arifî.
The text of this manuscript was rendered in a delicate cut paper découpage calligraphy by Mehmed bin Gazanfer and completed in
1540, and features many marbled and decorative paper borders. One early master by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pseudonym"] pseudonym of Şebek is mentioned
posthumously in the earliest Ottoman text on the art known as the Tertib-i Risâle-i Ebrî, which is dated based on internal evidence
to after 1615. The instructions for several ebru techniques in the text are accredited to this master. Another famous 18th-century
Page 22
master by the name of Hatip Mehmed Efendi (died 1773) is accredited with developing
motifs and perhaps early floral designs, although evidence from India appears to contradict
some of these reports. Despite this, marbled motifs are commonly referred to as hatip
designs in Turkey today.[462]
Literature and theatre 
 Turkish literature is a mix of cultural influences. Interaction
between the Ottoman Empire and the Islamic world along
with Europe contributed to a blend of Turkic, Islamic and
European traditions in modern-day Turkish music and
literary arts.[465] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_literature"] Turkish literature was heavily influenced
by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_literature"] Persian and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_literature"] Arabic literature during most of the Ottoman
era. 
 Ottoman miniature which can be
linked to the Persian miniature
tradition,[461] as well as strong
Chinese artistic influences.
 Namık Kemal's works had a
profound influence on
 Atatürk and other Turkish
statesmen who established
the Turkish
Republic.[463][464] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanzimat"] Tanzimat reforms of the 19th century introduced previously unknown Western genres,
primarily the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Novel"] novel and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Short_story"] short story. Many of the writers in the Tanzimat period wrote in several
genres simultaneously: for instance, the poet [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Namik_Kemal"] Nâmık Kemal also wrote the important 1876 novel
İntibâh (Awakening), while the journalist [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%B0brahim_%C5%9Einasi"] Şinasi has written, in 1860, the first modern Turkish play,
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One_act_play"] one-act comedy "Şair Evlenmesi" (The Poet's Marriage). Most of the roots of modern Turkish
literature were formed between the years 1896 and 1923. Broadly, there were three primary literary
movements during this period: the Edebiyat-ı Cedîde (New Literature) movement; the Fecr-i Âtî
(Dawn of the Future) movement; and the Millî Edebiyat (National Literature) movement.
The first radical step of innovation in 20th century Turkish
poetry was taken by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/N%C3%A2z%C4%B1m_Hikmet_Ran"] Nâzım Hikmet, who introduced the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_verse"] free verse style. Another
 revolution in Turkish poetry came about in 1941 with the Garip movement led by Orhan
Veli, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oktay_R%C4%B1fat_Horozcu"] Oktay Rıfat and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melih_Cevdet_Anday"] Melih Cevdet. The mix of cultural influences in Turkey is dramatised,
for example, in the form of the "new symbols of the clash and interlacing of cultures"
enacted in the novels of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orhan_Pamuk"] Orhan Pamuk, recipient of the 2006 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature"] Nobel Prize in Literature.[466]
The origin of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_theatre"] Turkish theatre dates back to ancient pagan rituals and oral legends. The
dances, music and songs performed during the rituals of the inhabitants of Anatolia
millennia ago are the elements from which the first shows originated. In time, the ancient
rituals, myths, legends and stories evolved into theatrical shows. Starting from the 11th-
century, the traditions of the Seljuk Turks blended with those of the indigenous peoples of
Anatolia and the interaction between diverse cultures paved the way for new plays. 
Nobel-laureate Turkish novelist
 Orhan Pamuk and his Turkish
Angora cat at his personal writing
space
After the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanzimat"] Tanzimat (Reformation) period in the 19th century, characters in Turkish theatre
were modernised and plays were performed on European-style stages, with actors wearing
 European costumes. Following the restoration of constitutional monarchy with the Young
Turk Revolution in 1908, theatrical activities increased and social problems began to be
 reflected at the theatre as well as in historical plays. A theatrical conservatoire, Darülbedayi-
i Osmani (which became the nucleus of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul_City_Theatres"] Istanbul City Theatres) was established in
1914. During the years of chaos and war, the Darülbedayi-i Osmani continued its activities
and attracted the younger generation. Numerous Turkish playwrights emerged in this era;
some of them wrote on romantic subjects, while others were interested in social problems,
and still others dealt with nationalistic themes. The first Turkish musicals were also written
in this period. In time, Turkish women began to appear on stage, which was an important
development in the late Ottoman society. Until then, female roles had only been played by
actresses who were members of Turkey's ethnic minorities. Today there are numerous
private theatres in the country, together with those which are subsidised by the government,
such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_State_Theatres"] Turkish State Theatres.[467] 
 Süreyya Opera House is situated in
the Asian side of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul"] Istanbul and
 Atatürk Cultural Center is the main
Opera House in the European side of
the city.
Music and dance
 Music of Turkey includes mainly Turkic elements as well as partial influences ranging from Central Asian folk music, Arabic
music, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_music"] Greek music, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_music"] Ottoman music, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_traditional_music"] Persian music and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_of_Southeastern_Europe"] Balkan music, as well as references to more modern European and
 American [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_music"] popular music. The roots of traditional music in Turkey span across centuries to a time when the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seljuk_Turks"] Seljuk Turks migrated to
 Anatolia and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persia"] Persia in the 11th century and contains elements of both Turkic and pre-Turkic influences. Much of its modern
popular music can trace its roots to the emergence in the early 1930s drive for Westernization.[469]
Page 23
With the assimilation of immigrants from various regions the diversity of musical genres
and musical instrumentation also expanded. Turkey has also seen documented folk music
and recorded popular music produced in the ethnic styles of Greek, Armenian, Albanian,
 Polish and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish"] Jewish communities, among others.[470]
Many Turkish cities and towns have vibrant local music scenes which, in turn, support a
 number of regional musical styles. Despite this however, western music styles like pop
music and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kanto_(music)"] kanto lost popularity to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabesque"] arabesque in the late 1970s and 1980s. It became popular
again by the beginning of the 1990s, as a result of an opening economy and society. With
the support of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sezen_Aksu"] Sezen Aksu, the resurging popularity of pop music gave rise to several
international Turkish pop stars such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ajda_Pekkan"] Ajda Pekkan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tarkan_(singer)"] Tarkan and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sertab_Erener"] Sertab Erener.
 Internationally acclaimed Turkish jazz and blues musicians and composers include Ahmet
Ertegun (founder and president of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_Records"] Atlantic Records), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/N%C3%BCkhet_Ruacan"] Nükhet Ruacan and Kerem Görsev.
Referred to as Süperstar by the
Turkish media, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ajda_Pekkan"] Ajda Pekkan is a
 prominent figure of Turkish pop
music, with a career spanning
decades and a repertoire of diverse
musical styles.[468] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Five"] Turkish Five is a name used by some authors
to identify the five pioneers of Western classical
music in Turkey, namely [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmed_Adnan_Saygun"] Ahmed Adnan Saygun,
 Ulvi Cemal Erkin, Cemal Reşit Rey, Hasan Ferit
Alnar and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Necil_Kaz%C4%B1m_Akses"] Necil Kazım Akses.[471] Internationally
acclaimed Turkish musicians of Western classical
music include pianists [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%B0dil_Biret"] İdil Biret, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Verda_Erman"] Verda Erman,
 Gülsin Onay, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pekinel_sisters"] Pekinel sisters (Güher and Süher
Pekinel), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ay%C5%9Feg%C3%BCl_Sar%C4%B1ca"] Ayşegül Sarıca and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faz%C4%B1l_Say"] Fazıl Say; violinists [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ayla_Erduran"] Ayla Erduran and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suna_Kan"] Suna Kan; opera
singers [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semiha_Berksoy"] Semiha Berksoy, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leyla_Gencer"] Leyla Gencer and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%BCne%C5%9F_G%C3%BCrle"] Güneş Gürle; and conductors [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emre_Arac%C4%B1"] Emre Aracı,
 Gürer Aykal, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erol_Erdin%C3%A7"] Erol Erdinç, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rengim_G%C3%B6kmen"] Rengim Gökmen and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hikmet_%C5%9Eim%C5%9Fek"] Hikmet Şimşek. 
 Barış Manço was a Turkish rock
musician and one of the founders of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolian_rock"] Anatolian rock genre.
 Turkish folk dance is diverse. Hora is performed in East Thrace; Zeybek in the Aegean Region, Southern Marmara and East-
Central Anatolia Region; Teke in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_Region"] Western Mediterranean Region; Kaşık Oyunları and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kar%C5%9F%C4%B1lama"] Karşılama in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Anatolia_Region"] West-Central Anatolia,
 Western Black Sea Region, Southern Marmara Region and Eastern Mediterranean Region; Horon in the Central and Eastern Black
 Sea Region; Halay in Eastern Anatolia and the Central Anatolia Region; and Bar and Lezginka in the Northeastern Anatolia
Region.[472]
Architecture
The Byzantine era is usually dated from 330 AD, when Constantine the Great moved the Roman capital to Byzantium, which
became Constantinople, until the fall of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire"] Byzantine Empire in 1453. Its architecture dramatically influenced the later medieval
architecture throughout Europe and the Near East, and became the primary progenitor of the Renaissance and Ottoman
architectural traditions that followed its collapse.[473] When the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire"] Roman Empire went Christian (as well as Eastwards) with its new
capital at Constantinople, its architecture became more sensuous and more ambitious. This new style would come to be known as
Byzantine with increasingly exotic domes and ever-richer mosaics, traveled west to Ravenna and Venice and as far north as
Moscow.[474]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seljuk_architecture"] architecture of the Seljuk Turks combined the elements and characteristics of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Architecture_of_Central_Asia"] Turkic architecture of Central Asia with those
of Persian, Arab, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_architecture"] Armenian and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_architecture"] Byzantine architecture. The transition from Seljuk architecture to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_architecture"] Ottoman architecture is most
 visible in Bursa, which was the capital of the Ottoman State between 1335 and 1413. Following the Ottoman conquest of
Constantinople (Istanbul) in 1453, Ottoman architecture was significantly influenced by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_architecture"] Byzantine architecture. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace"] Topkapı Palace in
 Istanbul is one of the most famous examples of classical Ottoman architecture and was the primary residence of the Ottoman
Sultans for approximately 400 years.[475] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mimar_Sinan"] Mimar Sinan (c.1489–1588) was the most important architect of the classical period in
 Ottoman architecture. He was the chief architect of at least 374 buildings that were constructed in various provinces of the Ottoman
Empire in the 16th century.[476] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedefkar_Mehmed_Agha"] Sedefkar Mehmed Agha also known as the architect of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Mosque,_Istanbul"] Blue Mosque was an Albanian origin
Devshirme. He became a pupil of architect Mimar Sinan, becoming his first assistant in charge of the office in the absence of Sinan.
His work heavily influenced by his teacher [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mimar_Sinan"] Mimar Sinan
Since the 18th century, Turkish architecture has been increasingly influenced by European styles, and this can be particularly seen
in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanzimat"] Tanzimat era buildings of Istanbul like the Dolmabahçe, Çırağan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taksim_Military_Barracks"] Taksim Military Barracks (demolished), Feriye, Beylerbeyi,
Küçüksu, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ihlamur_Palace"] Ihlamur and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Y%C4%B1ld%C4%B1z_Palace"] Yıldız palaces, which were all designed by members of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balyan_family"] Balyan family of Ottoman Armenian court
architects.[477] The Ottoman era [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yal%C4%B1"] waterfront houses (yalı) on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosphorus"] Bosphorus also reflect the fusion between classical Ottoman and
European architectural styles during the aforementioned period. Italian architect, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raimondo_D%27Aronco"] Raimondo D'Aronco served as the chief palace
architect to the Ottoman Sultan Abdülhamid II in Istanbul for 16 years. D'Aronco designed and built a large number of buildings of
various types in Istanbul. The stylistic features of his works can be classified in three groups: Revivalism, reinterpretation of the
Ottoman forms, Art Nouveau and Vienna Secession. Art Nouveau was first introduced to Istanbul by D'Aronco, and his designs
reveal that he drew freely on Byzantine and Ottoman decorations. He also mixed Western and Oriental styles in his work.
Page 24
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_National_Architectural_Movement"] First National Architectural Movement in the early 20th century sought to create a new
architecture, which was based on motifs from Seljuk and Ottoman architecture. The leading
architects of this movement were [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vedat_Tek"] Vedat Tek (1873–1942), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mimar_Kemaleddin_Bey"] Mimar Kemaleddin Bey (1870–
1927),  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arif_Hikmet_Koyuno%C4%9Flu"] Arif Hikmet Koyunoğlu (1888–1982) and Giulio Mongeri (1873–1953).[478]
 Buildings from this era are the Grand Post Office in Istanbul (1905–1909),  Tayyare
 Apartments (1919–1922),[479] Istanbul 4th Vakıf Han (1911–1926),[480] State Art and
Sculpture Museum (1927–1930),[481] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnography_Museum_of_Ankara"] Ethnography Museum of Ankara (1925–1928),[482] the
first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ziraat_Bank"] Ziraat Bank headquarters in Ankara (1925–1929),[483] the first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T%C3%BCrkiye_%C4%B0%C5%9F_Bankas%C4%B1"] Türkiye İş Bankası
headquarters in Ankara (1926–1929),[484] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bebek,_Istanbul"] Bebek Mosque,[485] and Kamer Hatun
Mosque.[486][487]
 Some of the notable contemporary architects of Turkey are Behruz Çinici, Emre Arolat, Murat
Tabanlıoğlu, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tabanl%C4%B1o%C4%9Flu_Architects"] Melkan Tabanlıoğlu, Melike Altınışık and Mehmet Kütükçüoğlu 
 Blue Mosque (1616) in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul"] Istanbul
Cuisine
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_cuisine"] Turkish cuisine is largely the heritage of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_cuisine"] Ottoman cuisine. In the early years of the Republic, a
few studies were published about regional Anatolian dishes but cuisine did not feature heavily
in Turkish folkloric studies until the 1980s, when the fledgling tourism industry encouraged
the Turkish state to sponsor two food symposia. The papers submitted at the symposia
presented the history of Turkish cuisine on a "historical continuum" that dated back to Turkic
origins in Central Asia and continued through the Seljuk and Ottoman periods.[492] 
 Çırağan Palace (1867) in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul"] Istanbul
Many of the papers presented at these first two symposia were unreferenced. Prior to the
symposia, the study of Turkish culinary culture was first popularised by the publication of
Süheyl Ünver's Fifty Dishes in Turkish History in 1948. This book was based on recipes
found in an 18th century Ottoman manuscript. His second book was about palace cuisine
during the reign of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehmet_II"] Mehmet II. Following the publication of Ünver's book subsequent studies
 were published, including a 1978 study by a historian named Bahaettin Ögel about the Central
Asian origins of Turkish cuisine.[492]
 Ottoman cuisine contains elements of Turkish, Byzantine, Balkan, Armenian, Kurdish, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_cuisine"] Arab
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_cuisine"] Persian cuisines.[493] The country's  position between Europe, Asia, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul_Main_Post_Office"] Grand Post Office (1909) in
Mediterranean Sea helped the Turks in gaining complete control of the major [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade_route"] trade routes, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul"] Istanbul
an ideal landscape and climate allowed plants and animals to flourish. Turkish cuisine was
well established by the mid-1400s, the beginning of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire"] Ottoman Empire's six hundred-year
reign. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yogurt"] Yogurt salads, fish in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olive_oil"] olive oil, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharbat"] sherbet and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dolma"] stuffed and wrapped vegetables became
Turkish staples. The empire, eventually spanning from Austria and Ukraine to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabia"] Arabia and
North Africa, used its land and water routes to import exotic ingredients from all over the
world. By the end of the 16th century, the Ottoman court housed over 1,400 live-in cooks and
passed laws regulating the freshness of food. Since the fall of the empire in World War I (1914–1918) and the establishment of the
Turkish Republic in 1923, foreign food such as French hollandaise sauce and Western fast food have made their way into the
modern Turkish diet.[494]
Sports
The most popular [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sports_in_Turkey"] sport in Turkey is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Association_football"] association football.[495] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)"] Galatasaray won the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000_UEFA_Cup_Final"] UEFA Cup and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000_UEFA_Super_Cup"] UEFA Super Cup in 2000.[496]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_national_football_team"] Turkish national football team won the bronze medal at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup"] 2002 FIFA World Cup, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_FIFA_Confederations_Cup"] 2003 FIFA Confederations Cup and
 UEFA Euro 2008.[497]
Other mainstream sports such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basketball"] basketball and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volleyball"] volleyball are also popular. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey_national_basketball_team"] men's national basketball team won the silver
medal at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_FIBA_World_Championship"] 2010 FIBA World Championship and at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EuroBasket_2001"] EuroBasket 2001, which were both hosted by Turkey; and is one of the most
successful at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basketball_at_the_Mediterranean_Games"] Mediterranean Games. Turkish basketball club [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fenerbah%C3%A7e_Men%27s_Basketball"] Fenerbahçe reached the final of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EuroLeague"] EuroLeague in three
consecutive seasons (2016, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_EuroLeague"] 2017 and 2018), becoming the European champions in 2017 and runners-up in 2016 and 2018.
Another Turkish basketball club, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anadolu_Efes_S.K."] Anadolu Efes S.K. won the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_EuroLeague"] 2020–21 EuroLeague and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_FIBA_Kora%C4%87_Cup"] 1995–96 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIBA_Kora%C4%87_Cup"] FIBA Korać Cup, were the
runners-up of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_EuroLeague"] 2018–19 EuroLeague and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_FIBA_European_Cup"] 1992–93 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIBA_Saporta_Cup"] FIBA Saporta Cup, and finished third at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_FIBA_EuroLeague"] 1999–2000 EuroLeague and
 the 2000–01 SuproLeague.[498][499] Beşiktaş won the 2011–12 FIBA EuroChallenge,[500] and Galatasaray won the 2015–16
Eurocup. The Final of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_EuroLeague_Women"] 2013–14 EuroLeague Women basketball championship was played between two Turkish teams,
 Galatasaray and Fenerbahçe, and won by Galatasaray.[501] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey_women%27s_national_basketball_team"] women's national basketball team won the silver medal at the
 EuroBasket Women 2011 and the bronze medal at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EuroBasket_Women_2013"] EuroBasket Women 2013. Like the men's team, the women's basketball team
is one of the most successful at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basketball_at_the_Mediterranean_Games"] Mediterranean Games.
Page 25
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey_women%27s_national_volleyball_team"] women's national volleyball team won the gold medal at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_European_Games"] 2015 European Games, the
 silver medal at the 2003 European Championship, the bronze medal at the 2011 European
Championship, and the bronze medal at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_FIVB_World_Grand_Prix"] 2012 FIVB World Grand Prix. They also won
multiple medals over multiple decades at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_Mediterranean_Games"] Mediterranean Games.[506] Women's volleyball
clubs, namely Fenerbahçe, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eczac%C4%B1ba%C5%9F%C4%B1_Istanbul"] Eczacıbaşı and Vakıfbank, have won numerous European
 championship titles and medals. Fenerbahçe won the 2010 FIVB Women's Club World
Championship and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CEV_Women%27s_Champions_League"] 2012 CEV Women's Champions League. Representing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Volleyball_Confederation"] Europe as the
winner of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_CEV_Women%27s_Champions_League"] 2012–13 CEV Women's Champions League, Vakıfbank also became the world
champion by winning the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013_FIVB_Volleyball_Women%27s_Club_World_Championship"] 2013 FIVB Volleyball Women's Club World Championship.
Recently Vakıfbank has won the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Women%27s_Club_World_Championship"] FIVB Volleyball Women's Club World Championship in
 2017 and 2018,[502][503][504] and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_CEV_Women%27s_Champions_League"] 2017–18 CEV Women's Champions League for the
fourth time in their history.[505] 
 Turkish coffee with Turkish
delight. Turkish coffee is a
 UNESCO-listed intangible cultural
heritage of Turks.[488][489]
The traditional national sport of Turkey has been [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oil_wrestling"] yağlı güreş ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olive_oil"] oil [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wrestling"] wrestling) since Ottoman
times.[507] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edirne_Province"] Edirne Province has hosted the annual [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C4%B1rkp%C4%B1nar"] Kırkpınar oil wrestling tournament since
1361, making it the oldest continuously held sporting competition in the world.[508][509] In the
19th and early 20th centuries, Ottoman Turkish oil wrestling champions such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yusuf_%C4%B0smail"] Koca Yusuf,
 Nurullah Hasan and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lc%C4%B1kl%C4%B1_Mahmut"] Kızılcıklı Mahmut acquired international fame in Europe and North
America by winning world heavyweight wrestling championship titles. International wrestling
styles governed by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Federation_of_Associated_Wrestling_Styles"] FILA such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freestyle_wrestling"] freestyle wrestling and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Roman_wrestling"] Greco-Roman wrestling are also
popular, with many European, World and Olympic championship titles won by Turkish
wrestlers both individually and as a national team.[510]

 Turkish television dramas are increasingly becoming popular beyond Turkey's borders and
are among the country's most vital exports, both in terms of profit and public

 Yeşilçam is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sobriquet"] sobriquet that refers to the
Turkish film art and industry. The first
 movie exhibited in the Ottoman Empire was the Lumiere Brothers' 1895 film, L'Arrivée
d'un train en gare de La Ciotat, which was shown in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul"] Istanbul in 1896. The first Turkish-
made film was a documentary entitled [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ayastefanos%27taki_Rus_Abidesinin_Y%C4%B1k%C4%B1l%C4%B1%C5%9F%C4%B1"] Ayastefanos'taki Rus Abidesinin Yıkılışı (Demolition
of the Russian Monument at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ye%C5%9Filk%C3%B6y"] San Stefano), directed by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fuat_Uzk%C4%B1nay"] Fuat Uzkınay and completed in
1914. The first narrative film, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedat_Simavi"] Sedat Simavi's The Spy, was released in 1917. Turkey's first
sound film was shown in 1931. Turkish directors like [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metin_Erksan"] Metin Erksan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuri_Bilge_Ceylan"] Nuri Bilge Ceylan,
 Yılmaz Güney, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zeki_Demirkubuz"] Zeki Demirkubuz and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferzan_%C3%96zpetek"] Ferzan Özpetek won numerous international awards
such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palme_d%27Or"] Palme d'Or and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Bear"] Golden Bear.[519][520] 
The closing ceremony of the annual
 International Antalya Golden Orange
Despite legal provisions, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_freedom_in_Turkey"] media freedom in Turkey has steadily deteriorated from 2010
onwards, with a precipitous decline following the failed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_Turkish_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt"] coup attempt on 15 July 2016.[521] 
Film Festival takes place at the
 Aspendos amphitheatre.
As of December 2016, at least 81 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_arrested_journalists_in_Turkey"] journalists were imprisoned in Turkey and more than 100
Page 26
 news outlets were closed.[266] Freedom House lists Turkey's media as not free.[522] The media crackdowns also extend to Internet
censorship with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_block_of_Wikipedia_in_Turkey"] Wikipedia getting blocked between 29 April 2017 and 15 January 2020.[523][524]

a. Turkish President Recep Tayyip Erdogan has said "Our attitude on the Armenian issue has been clear from the
beginning. We will never accept the accusations of genocide".[23] Scholars give several reasons for Turkey's
 position including the preservation of national identity, the demand for reparations and territorial concerns.[24]
